     <p>The <b>University of Maryland, College Park</b> (often referred to as <b>The University of Maryland</b>, <b>Maryland</b>, <b>UM</b>, <b>UMD</b>, or <b>UMCP</b> ) is a public research university<sup id="cite_ref-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-7"><span>[</span>7<span>]</span></a></sup> located in the city of <a href="/wiki/College_Park,_Maryland" title="College Park, Maryland">College Park</a> in <a href="/wiki/Prince_George%27s_County" title="Prince George's County" class="mw-redirect">Prince George's County</a>, <a href="/wiki/Maryland" title="Maryland">Maryland</a>, just outside Washington, D.C. Founded in 1856, the University of Maryland is the flagship institution of the <a href="/wiki/University_System_of_Maryland" title="University System of Maryland">University System of Maryland</a>. It is considered a <a href="/wiki/Public_Ivy" title="Public Ivy">Public Ivy</a> institution. With a fall 2010 enrollment of more than 37,000 students, over 100 undergraduate majors and 120 graduate programs, Maryland is the largest university in the state and the largest in the <a href="/wiki/Washington_Metropolitan_Area" title="Washington Metropolitan Area" class="mw-redirect">Washington Metropolitan Area</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-umfacts_6-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-umfacts-6"><span>[</span>6<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-8" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-8"><span>[</span>8<span>]</span></a></sup> It is a member of the <a href="/wiki/Association_of_American_Universities" title="Association of American Universities">Association of American Universities</a> and a founding member of the <a href="/wiki/Atlantic_Coast_Conference" title="Atlantic Coast Conference">Atlantic Coast Conference</a> athletic league.</p> 
     <p>The University of Maryland's proximity to the nation's capital has resulted in strong research partnerships with the <a href="/wiki/Federal_government_of_the_United_States" title="Federal government of the United States">Federal government</a>. Many members of the faculty receive research funding and institutional support from agencies such as the <a href="/wiki/National_Institutes_of_Health" title="National Institutes of Health">National Institutes of Health</a>, the <a href="/wiki/National_Aeronautics_and_Space_Administration" title="National Aeronautics and Space Administration" class="mw-redirect">National Aeronautics and Space Administration</a> (NASA), the <a href="/wiki/National_Institute_of_Standards_and_Technology" title="National Institute of Standards and Technology">National Institute of Standards and Technology</a> and the <a href="/wiki/United_States_Department_of_Homeland_Security" title="United States Department of Homeland Security">Department of Homeland Security</a>.</p> 
     <p>The operating budget of the University of Maryland, College Park, in <a href="/wiki/Fiscal_year" title="Fiscal year">fiscal year</a> 2009 was projected to be approximately US$1.531 billion.<sup id="cite_ref-9" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-9"><span>[</span>9<span>]</span></a></sup> For the same fiscal year, the University of Maryland received a total of $518 million in research funding, surpassing its 2008 mark by $117 million.<sup id="cite_ref-10" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-10"><span>[</span>10<span>]</span></a></sup> As of May 11, 2012, the university's &quot;Great Expectations&quot; campaign had exceeded $950 million in private donations.<sup id="cite_ref-11" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-11"><span>[</span>11<span>]</span></a></sup></p>

        <td> 
         <div id="toctitle">

     <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="History">History</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_Maryland,_College_Park&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: History">edit</a>]</span></h2> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Early_history">Early history</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_Maryland,_College_Park&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Early history">edit</a>]</span></h3> 
     <p>On March 6, 1856, the forerunner of today's University of Maryland was chartered as the <b>Maryland Agricultural College</b> (1856?1916). Two years later, <a href="/wiki/Charles_Benedict_Calvert" title="Charles Benedict Calvert">Charles Benedict Calvert</a>, a descendant of the <a href="/wiki/Baron_Baltimore" title="Baron Baltimore">Barons Baltimore</a>, fervent believer in agricultural education, and a future U.S. Congressman, purchased 420 acres (1.7&nbsp;km<sup>2</sup>) of the <a href="/wiki/Riversdale_(Maryland)" title="Riversdale (Maryland)" class="mw-redirect">Riverdale Plantation</a> in College Park for $21,000. Calvert founded the school later that year with money earned by the sale of stock certificates. On October 5, 1859, the first 34 students entered the Maryland Agricultural College, including four of Charles Calvert's sons, George, Charles, William and Eugene. The keynote speaker on opening day was Joseph Henry, the first Secretary of the Smithsonian Institution. <sup id="cite_ref-umtimeline_12-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-umtimeline-12"><span>[</span>12<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p><br /></p> 
     <div class="thumb tright"> 
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;">
       <a href="/wiki/File:Charles_Benedict_Calvert_-_photo_portrait_seated.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c2/Charles_Benedict_Calvert_-_photo_portrait_seated.jpg/170px-Charles_Benedict_Calvert_-_photo_portrait_seated.jpg" width="170" height="222" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c2/Charles_Benedict_Calvert_-_photo_portrait_seated.jpg/255px-Charles_Benedict_Calvert_-_photo_portrait_seated.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c2/Charles_Benedict_Calvert_-_photo_portrait_seated.jpg/340px-Charles_Benedict_Calvert_-_photo_portrait_seated.jpg 2x" /></a> 
       <div class="thumbcaption"> 
        <div class="magnify">
         <a href="/wiki/File:Charles_Benedict_Calvert_-_photo_portrait_seated.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"><img src="//bits.wikimedia.org/static-1.22wmf9/skins/common/images/magnify-clip.png" width="15" height="11" alt="" /></a>
        </div> 
        <a href="/wiki/Charles_Benedict_Calvert" title="Charles Benedict Calvert">Charles Benedict Calvert</a>, founder
       </div> 
      </div> 
     </div> 
     <p>In July 1862, the same month that the Maryland Agricultural College awarded its first degrees, <a href="/wiki/Abraham_Lincoln" title="Abraham Lincoln">President Lincoln</a> signed the <a href="/wiki/Morrill_Land_Grant_Act" title="Morrill Land Grant Act" class="mw-redirect">Morrill Land Grant Act</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-13" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-13"><span>[</span>13<span>]</span></a></sup> The legislation provided federal funds to schools that taught agriculture or engineering, or provided military training. Taking advantage of the opportunity, the school became a <a href="/wiki/Land_grant_college" title="Land grant college" class="mw-redirect">land grant college</a> in February 1864 after the Maryland legislature voted to approve the Morrill Act.<sup id="cite_ref-umtimeline_12-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-umtimeline-12"><span>[</span>12<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Civil_War">Civil War</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_Maryland,_College_Park&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Civil War">edit</a>]</span></h3> 
     <p>A few months after accepting the grant, the Maryland Agricultural College proved to be an important site in the <a href="/wiki/American_Civil_War" title="American Civil War">Civil War</a>. In April 1864, General <a href="/wiki/Ambrose_Burnside" title="Ambrose Burnside">Ambrose E. Burnside</a> and 6,000 soldiers of the Union's Ninth Army Corps camped on the MAC campus. The troops were en route to reinforce General <a href="/wiki/Ulysses_S_Grant" title="Ulysses S Grant" class="mw-redirect">Ulysses S. Grant</a>'s forces in <a href="/wiki/Virginia" title="Virginia">Virginia</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-14" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-14"><span>[</span>14<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>Later that summer, around 400 Confederate soldiers led by General <a href="/wiki/Bradley_T._Johnson" title="Bradley T. Johnson" class="mw-redirect">Bradley T. Johnson</a> stayed on the grounds while preparing to take part in a raid against Washington. A local legend claims that soldiers were warmly welcomed by university President Henry Onderdonk, a Confederate sympathizer, and that the cavalrymen were thrown a party on the campus nicknamed &quot;The Old South Ball.&quot; The next morning the soldiers rode off to cut the lines of communication between Washington and Baltimore.<sup id="cite_ref-15" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-15"><span>[</span>15<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>Financial problems forced the increasingly desperate administrators to sell off 200 acres (81&nbsp;ha) of land, and the continuing decline in student enrollment sent the Maryland Agricultural College into bankruptcy. For the next two years the campus was used as a boys preparatory school.<sup id="cite_ref-umtimeline_12-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-umtimeline-12"><span>[</span>12<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <div class="thumb tright"> 
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a href="/wiki/File:UMD_Morrill_Hall.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d9/UMD_Morrill_Hall.JPG/220px-UMD_Morrill_Hall.JPG" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d9/UMD_Morrill_Hall.JPG/330px-UMD_Morrill_Hall.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d9/UMD_Morrill_Hall.JPG/440px-UMD_Morrill_Hall.JPG 2x" /></a> 
       <div class="thumbcaption"> 
        <div class="magnify">
         <a href="/wiki/File:UMD_Morrill_Hall.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"><img src="//bits.wikimedia.org/static-1.22wmf9/skins/common/images/magnify-clip.png" width="15" height="11" alt="" /></a>
        </div> 
        <a href="/wiki/Morrill_Hall_(University_of_Maryland)" title="Morrill Hall (University of Maryland)">Morrill Hall</a>, built in 1898, is the oldest academic building on campus.
       </div> 
      </div> 
     </div> 
     <p>Following the Civil War, the Maryland legislature pulled the college out of bankruptcy, and in February 1866 assumed half ownership of the school. The college thus became in part a state institution. <a href="/wiki/George_Washington_Custis_Lee" title="George Washington Custis Lee">George Washington Custis Lee</a>, son of Confederate General <a href="/wiki/Robert_E_Lee" title="Robert E Lee" class="mw-redirect">Robert E. Lee</a>, was appointed president of the college by the Board of Trustees, but due to public outcry declined the position. By October 1867, the school reopened with 11 students. In the next six years, enrollment continued to grow, and the school's debt was finally paid off. Twenty years later, the school's reputation as a research institution began, as the federally funded Agricultural Experiment Station was established there. During the same period, a number of state laws granted the college regulatory powers in several areas?including controlling farm disease, inspecting feed, establishing a state weather bureau and geological survey, and housing the board of forestry.<sup id="cite_ref-umtimeline_12-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-umtimeline-12"><span>[</span>12<span>]</span></a></sup> In 1888, the college began its first official intercollegiate baseball games against rivals <a href="/wiki/St._John%27s_College_(Annapolis/Santa_Fe)" title="St. John's College (Annapolis/Santa Fe)">St. John's College</a> and the <a href="/wiki/United_States_Naval_Academy" title="United States Naval Academy">United States Naval Academy</a>. Baseball, however, had been played at the college for decades before the first &quot;official&quot; games were recorded. The first fraternity chapter at Maryland, the Eta chapter of <a href="/wiki/Phi_Sigma_Kappa" title="Phi Sigma Kappa">Phi Sigma Kappa</a>, was established in 1897, and <a href="/wiki/Morrill_Hall_(University_of_Maryland)" title="Morrill Hall (University of Maryland)">Morrill Hall</a> (the oldest instructional building still in use on campus) was built the following year.<sup id="cite_ref-umtimeline_12-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-umtimeline-12"><span>[</span>12<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="The_Great_Fire_of_1912">The Great Fire of 1912</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_Maryland,_College_Park&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: The Great Fire of 1912">edit</a>]</span></h3> 
     <div class="thumb tright"> 
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a href="/wiki/File:MAC_fire_1912.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/c/c4/MAC_fire_1912.jpg/220px-MAC_fire_1912.jpg" width="220" height="102" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/c/c4/MAC_fire_1912.jpg/330px-MAC_fire_1912.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/c/c4/MAC_fire_1912.jpg/440px-MAC_fire_1912.jpg 2x" /></a> 
       <div class="thumbcaption"> 
        <div class="magnify">
         <a href="/wiki/File:MAC_fire_1912.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"><img src="//bits.wikimedia.org/static-1.22wmf9/skins/common/images/magnify-clip.png" width="15" height="11" alt="" /></a>
        </div> The campus ablaze during the 1912 fire
       </div> 
      </div> 
     </div> 
     <div class="thumb tright"> 
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a href="/wiki/File:1912Fire.jpeg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6c/1912Fire.jpeg/220px-1912Fire.jpeg" width="220" height="125" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6c/1912Fire.jpeg/330px-1912Fire.jpeg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6c/1912Fire.jpeg/440px-1912Fire.jpeg 2x" /></a> 
       <div class="thumbcaption"> 
        <div class="magnify">
         <a href="/wiki/File:1912Fire.jpeg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"><img src="//bits.wikimedia.org/static-1.22wmf9/skins/common/images/magnify-clip.png" width="15" height="11" alt="" /></a>
        </div> The remains of the administration building.
       </div> 
      </div> 
     </div> 
     <div class="thumb tright"> 
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a href="/wiki/File:UMD_map_of_original_campus.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6a/UMD_map_of_original_campus.JPG/220px-UMD_map_of_original_campus.JPG" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6a/UMD_map_of_original_campus.JPG/330px-UMD_map_of_original_campus.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6a/UMD_map_of_original_campus.JPG/440px-UMD_map_of_original_campus.JPG 2x" /></a> 
       <div class="thumbcaption"> 
        <div class="magnify">
         <a href="/wiki/File:UMD_map_of_original_campus.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"><img src="//bits.wikimedia.org/static-1.22wmf9/skins/common/images/magnify-clip.png" width="15" height="11" alt="" /></a>
        </div> Plaque showing the original layout of campus before the Great Fire.
       </div> 
      </div> 
     </div> 
     <p>On November 29, 1912, around 10:30&nbsp;pm, a fire, probably due to faulty electric wiring, broke out in the attic of the newest administration building, where a <a href="/wiki/Thanksgiving" title="Thanksgiving">Thanksgiving</a> dance was being held. The approximately eighty students on the premises evacuated themselves safely, and then formed a makeshift bucket brigade. The fire departments summoned from nearby <a href="/wiki/Hyattsville,_Maryland" title="Hyattsville, Maryland">Hyattsville</a> and Washington, D.C., arrived too late. Fanned by a strong southwest wind, the fire destroyed the barracks where the students were housed, all the school's records, and most of the academic buildings, leaving only <a href="/wiki/Morrill_Hall_(University_of_Maryland)" title="Morrill Hall (University of Maryland)">Morrill Hall</a> untouched. The loss was estimated at $250,000 (about $5.8 million in 2012 U.S. dollars) despite no injuries or fatalities. The devastation was so great that many never expected the university to reopen. University President Richard Silvester resigned, brokenhearted.<sup id="cite_ref-umtimeline_12-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-umtimeline-12"><span>[</span>12<span>]</span></a></sup> However, the students refused to give up. All but two returned to the university after the break and insisted on classes continuing as usual. Students were housed by families in neighboring towns who were compensated by the university until housing could be rebuilt, although a new administration building was not built until the 1940s.<sup id="cite_ref-umtimeline_12-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-umtimeline-12"><span>[</span>12<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>A large brick and concrete compass inlaid in the ground designates the former center of campus as it existed in 1912. Lines engraved in the compass point to each building that was destroyed in the Thanksgiving Day fire. The intersection of the lines on the compass are known as &quot;The Point of Failure&quot;. A well-known legend holds that any student who walks upon the &quot;point of failure&quot; will not graduate.</p> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Modern_history">Modern history</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_Maryland,_College_Park&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Modern history">edit</a>]</span></h3> 
     <div class="thumb tright"> 
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a href="/wiki/File:Univ_of_Maryland_campus_1938.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/6/60/Univ_of_Maryland_campus_1938.jpg/220px-Univ_of_Maryland_campus_1938.jpg" width="220" height="146" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/6/60/Univ_of_Maryland_campus_1938.jpg/330px-Univ_of_Maryland_campus_1938.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/6/60/Univ_of_Maryland_campus_1938.jpg/440px-Univ_of_Maryland_campus_1938.jpg 2x" /></a> 
       <div class="thumbcaption"> 
        <div class="magnify">
         <a href="/wiki/File:Univ_of_Maryland_campus_1938.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"><img src="//bits.wikimedia.org/static-1.22wmf9/skins/common/images/magnify-clip.png" width="15" height="11" alt="" /></a>
        </div> The University of Maryland campus as it appeared in 1938 before the dramatic expansion engineered by 
        <a href="/wiki/Curley_Byrd" title="Curley Byrd">President Byrd</a>
       </div> 
      </div> 
     </div> 
     <p>The state took complete control of the school in 1916, and consequently the institution was renamed <b>Maryland State College</b> (1916?1920). Also that year, the first female students enrolled at the school. On April 9, 1920, the college merged with the established professional schools in <a href="/wiki/University_of_Maryland,_Baltimore" title="University of Maryland, Baltimore">Baltimore</a> to form the <b>University of Maryland</b> (1920 ? present). The graduate school on the College Park campus awarded its first PhD degrees, and the University's enrollment reached 500 students in the same year. In 1925 the University was accredited by the <a href="/wiki/Association_of_American_Universities" title="Association of American Universities">Association of American Universities</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-umtimeline_12-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-umtimeline-12"><span>[</span>12<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>During World War II, Maryland was one of 131 colleges and universities nationally that took part in the <a href="/wiki/V-12_Navy_College_Training_Program" title="V-12 Navy College Training Program">V-12 Navy College Training Program</a> which offered students a path to a Navy commission.<sup id="cite_ref-umaryland-v-12_16-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-umaryland-v-12-16"><span>[</span>16<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>By the time the first black students enrolled at the University in 1951, enrollment had grown to nearly 10,000 students?4,000 of whom were women. Prior to 1951, many black students in Maryland were enrolled at the <a href="/wiki/University_of_Maryland,_Eastern_Shore" title="University of Maryland, Eastern Shore" class="mw-redirect">University of Maryland, Eastern Shore</a>, which was almost shut down in 1947 due to lack of access, low quality education, and the fear among some black and white leaders that Eastern Shore was allowed to remain a college by the Regents of the University of Maryland solely to keep black students in segregated, inferior institutions.<sup id="cite_ref-17" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-17"><span>[</span>17<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>In 1957 President Wilson H. Elkins made a push to increase academic standards at the University. His efforts resulted in the creation of one of the first Academic Probation Plans. The first year the plan went into effect, 1,550 students (18% of the total student body) faced expulsion. Since then, academic standards at the school have steadily risen. Recognizing the improvement in academics, <a href="/wiki/Phi_Beta_Kappa" title="Phi Beta Kappa" class="mw-redirect">Phi Beta Kappa</a> established a chapter at the university in 1964. In 1969, the university was elected to the Association of American Universities. The school continued to grow, and by the fall of 1985 reached an enrollment of 38,679.<sup id="cite_ref-umtimeline_12-8" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-umtimeline-12"><span>[</span>12<span>]</span></a></sup> Like many colleges during the Vietnam War, the university was the site of student protests and had curfews enforced by the <a href="/wiki/Maryland_Army_National_Guard" title="Maryland Army National Guard">National Guard</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-18" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-18"><span>[</span>18<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <div class="thumb tleft"> 
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;">
       <a href="/wiki/File:Memorial_Chapel_at_UMCP,_front_view_off-center,_August_21,_2006.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/49/Memorial_Chapel_at_UMCP%2C_front_view_off-center%2C_August_21%2C_2006.jpg/170px-Memorial_Chapel_at_UMCP%2C_front_view_off-center%2C_August_21%2C_2006.jpg" width="170" height="228" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/49/Memorial_Chapel_at_UMCP%2C_front_view_off-center%2C_August_21%2C_2006.jpg/255px-Memorial_Chapel_at_UMCP%2C_front_view_off-center%2C_August_21%2C_2006.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/49/Memorial_Chapel_at_UMCP%2C_front_view_off-center%2C_August_21%2C_2006.jpg/340px-Memorial_Chapel_at_UMCP%2C_front_view_off-center%2C_August_21%2C_2006.jpg 2x" /></a> 
       <div class="thumbcaption"> 
        <div class="magnify">
         <a href="/wiki/File:Memorial_Chapel_at_UMCP,_front_view_off-center,_August_21,_2006.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"><img src="//bits.wikimedia.org/static-1.22wmf9/skins/common/images/magnify-clip.png" width="15" height="11" alt="" /></a>
        </div> 
        <a href="/wiki/Memorial_Chapel_(University_of_Maryland)" title="Memorial Chapel (University of Maryland)">Memorial Chapel</a>
       </div> 
      </div> 
     </div> 
     <p>In a massive 1988 restructuring of the state higher education system, the school was designated as the flagship campus of the newly formed <a href="/wiki/University_System_of_Maryland" title="University System of Maryland">University System of Maryland</a> and was formally named University of Maryland, College Park. However, in 1997 the <a href="/wiki/Maryland_General_Assembly" title="Maryland General Assembly">Maryland General Assembly</a> passed legislation allowing the University of Maryland, College Park, to be known simply as the University of Maryland, recognizing the campus' role as the flagship institution of the University System of Maryland.<sup id="cite_ref-19" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-19"><span>[</span>19<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>The other University System of Maryland institutions with the name &quot;University of Maryland&quot; are not satellite campuses of the University of Maryland, College Park, and are not referred to as such. The <a href="/wiki/University_of_Maryland,_Baltimore" title="University of Maryland, Baltimore">University of Maryland, Baltimore</a>, is the only other school permitted to confer certain degrees that state, simply &quot;University of Maryland&quot;. This is because the Baltimore school offers primarily graduate degrees in disciplines not taught at College Park, such as Nursing, Dentistry, Law and Medicine. The relationship between the University of Maryland, College Park, and the University of Maryland, Baltimore, is akin to the relationship of the University of California, Berkeley, to the University of California, San Francisco (UCSF), which also primarily offers graduate programs that Berkeley does not provide.</p> 
     <h4><span class="mw-headline" id="21st_century">21st century</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_Maryland,_College_Park&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: 21st century">edit</a>]</span></h4> 
     <div class="thumb tright"> 
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a href="/wiki/File:UMD_McKeldin_Library.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/01/UMD_McKeldin_Library.JPG/220px-UMD_McKeldin_Library.JPG" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/01/UMD_McKeldin_Library.JPG/330px-UMD_McKeldin_Library.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/01/UMD_McKeldin_Library.JPG/440px-UMD_McKeldin_Library.JPG 2x" /></a> 
       <div class="thumbcaption"> 
        <div class="magnify">
         <a href="/wiki/File:UMD_McKeldin_Library.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"><img src="//bits.wikimedia.org/static-1.22wmf9/skins/common/images/magnify-clip.png" width="15" height="11" alt="" /></a>
        </div> 
        <a href="/wiki/McKeldin_Library" title="McKeldin Library" class="mw-redirect">McKeldin Library</a>.
       </div> 
      </div> 
     </div> 
     <p>On September 24, 2001, a <a href="/wiki/Tornado" title="Tornado">tornado</a> struck the College Park campus, killing two female students and causing $15 million in damage to 12 buildings.<sup id="cite_ref-20" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-20"><span>[</span>20<span>]</span></a></sup> That same year brought the opening of the <a href="/wiki/Clarice_Smith_Performing_Arts_Center" title="Clarice Smith Performing Arts Center">Clarice Smith Performing Arts Center</a>, the largest single building ever constructed by the State of Maryland, which replaced <a href="/wiki/Tawes_Theatre" title="Tawes Theatre">Tawes Theatre</a> as the premier fine arts center on campus.<sup id="cite_ref-21" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-21"><span>[</span>21<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>In 2004, the university began constructing the 150-acre (61&nbsp;ha) &quot;M Square Research Park,&quot; which is the largest research park inside the <a href="/wiki/Capital_Beltway" title="Capital Beltway" class="mw-redirect">Capital Beltway</a>, and includes facilities affiliated with the <a href="/wiki/U.S._Department_of_Defense" title="U.S. Department of Defense" class="mw-redirect">U.S. Department of Defense</a>, <a href="/wiki/Food_and_Drug_Administration" title="Food and Drug Administration">Food and Drug Administration</a>, and the new National Center for Weather and Climate Prediction, affiliated with The <a href="/wiki/National_Oceanic_and_Atmospheric_Administration" title="National Oceanic and Atmospheric Administration">National Oceanic and Atmospheric Administration</a> (NOAA).<sup id="cite_ref-22" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-22"><span>[</span>22<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>The university launched its 7-year campaign to raise $1 billion dollars via private donations, called &quot;Great Expectations,&quot; in 2006.<sup id="cite_ref-23" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-23"><span>[</span>23<span>]</span></a></sup> The university published a new 10-year strategic plan in 2008,<sup id="cite_ref-24" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-24"><span>[</span>24<span>]</span></a></sup> which includes plans for the East Campus Redevelopment Project which would bring, among other things, on-campus graduate student housing and a state-of-the-art music and entertainment center to campus.<sup id="cite_ref-25" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-25"><span>[</span>25<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>In May 2010, ground was broken on a new $128-million, 158,068-square-foot (14,685.0&nbsp;m<sup>2</sup>) Physical Science Complex, including an <a href="/wiki/American_Recovery_and_Reinvestment_Act_of_2009" title="American Recovery and Reinvestment Act of 2009">ARRA</a>-funded advanced quantum science laboratory, which the university hopes will be the premier facility for such research in the world.<sup id="cite_ref-26" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-26"><span>[</span>26<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>The university's administration has recently become embroiled in the debate over the construction of a <a href="/wiki/Purple_Line_(Maryland)" title="Purple Line (Maryland)">light-rail line</a> through campus which would give the University another link to the <a href="/wiki/Dc_metro#Related_projects" title="Dc metro" class="mw-redirect">DC Metro</a> System.<sup id="cite_ref-27" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-27"><span>[</span>27<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-28" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-28"><span>[</span>28<span>]</span></a></sup> On August 16, 2010, <a href="/wiki/Wallace_Loh" title="Wallace Loh">Wallace Loh</a>, the Provost of the University of Iowa, was named President of the University effective November 1.<sup id="cite_ref-wp817_5-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-wp817-5"><span>[</span>5<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Academics">Academics</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_Maryland,_College_Park&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Academics">edit</a>]</span></h2> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Profile">Profile</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_Maryland,_College_Park&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Profile">edit</a>]</span></h3> 
     <p>The University of Maryland offers 127 undergraduate degrees and 112 graduate degrees in thirteen different colleges and schools:</p> 
     <table> 
      <tbody>
       <tr> 
        <td valign="top"> 
         <ul> 
          <li><a href="/wiki/A._James_Clark_School_of_Engineering" title="A. James Clark School of Engineering">A. James Clark School of Engineering</a></li> 
          <li><a href="/wiki/University_of_Maryland_College_of_Agriculture_and_Natural_Resources" title="University of Maryland College of Agriculture and Natural Resources">College of Agriculture and Natural Resources</a></li> 
          <li>College of Arts and Humanities 
           <ul> 
            <li><a href="/wiki/University_of_Maryland_School_of_Music" title="University of Maryland School of Music">School of Music</a></li> 
           </ul> </li> 
          <li><a href="/wiki/University_of_Maryland_College_of_Behavioral_and_Social_Sciences" title="University of Maryland College of Behavioral and Social Sciences">College of Behavioral and Social Sciences</a></li> 
          <li>College of Computer, Mathematical, and Natural Sciences</li> 
         </ul> </td> 
        <td valign="top"> 
         <ul> 
          <li>College of Education</li> 
          <li><a href="/wiki/University_of_Maryland_College_of_Information_Studies" title="University of Maryland College of Information Studies">College of Information Studies</a></li> 
          <li><a href="/wiki/Philip_Merrill_College_of_Journalism" title="Philip Merrill College of Journalism">Philip Merrill College of Journalism</a></li> 
          <li><a href="/wiki/Robert_H._Smith_School_of_Business" title="Robert H. Smith School of Business">Robert H. Smith School of Business</a></li> 
          <li><a href="/wiki/University_of_Maryland_School_of_Architecture" title="University of Maryland School of Architecture">School of Architecture, Planning &amp; Preservation</a></li> 
          <li>School of Public Health (formerly the College of Health &amp; Human Performance)</li> 
          <li>Office of Undergraduate Studies</li> 
          <li><a href="/wiki/University_of_Maryland_School_of_Public_Policy" title="University of Maryland School of Public Policy">School of Public Policy</a></li> 
         </ul> </td> 
       </tr> 
      </tbody>
     </table> 
     <p>Undergraduate education is centered around both a student's chosen academic program and the selection of core coursework to fulfill general education requirements.<sup id="cite_ref-29" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-29"><span>[</span>29<span>]</span></a></sup> For Spring 2010, the average undergraduate <a href="/wiki/GPA" title="GPA" class="mw-redirect">GPA</a> for women was 3.22 and 3.05 for undergraduate men.<sup id="cite_ref-30" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-30"><span>[</span>30<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Programs">Programs</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_Maryland,_College_Park&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Programs">edit</a>]</span></h3> 
     <div class="thumb tright"> 
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a href="/wiki/File:UMD_stairway.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/58/UMD_stairway.JPG/220px-UMD_stairway.JPG" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/58/UMD_stairway.JPG/330px-UMD_stairway.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/58/UMD_stairway.JPG/440px-UMD_stairway.JPG 2x" /></a> 
       <div class="thumbcaption"> 
        <div class="magnify">
         <a href="/wiki/File:UMD_stairway.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"><img src="//bits.wikimedia.org/static-1.22wmf9/skins/common/images/magnify-clip.png" width="15" height="11" alt="" /></a>
        </div> A stairway in south campus.
       </div> 
      </div> 
     </div> 
     <p>The university hosts &quot;Living and Learning&quot; programs which allow students with similar academic interests to live in the same residential community, take specialized courses, and perform research in those areas of expertise. An example is the University Honors College, which is geared towards students with exceptional academic talents. The Honors College welcomes students into a community of faculty and intellectually gifted undergraduates committed to acquiring a broad and balanced education. The Honors College offers seven living and learning programs: Advanced Cyber Security, Digital Cultures &amp; Creativity, Entrepreneurship and Innovation, Honors Humanities, Gemstone, Integrated Life Sciences, and University Honors.<sup id="cite_ref-31" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-31"><span>[</span>31<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>Digital Cultures and Creativity (DCC) is one of the six University of Maryland living and learning honors programs offered to incoming honors-level students. Started in 2009, the program is currently directed by technologically focused, interdisciplinary artist <a href="/wiki/Hasan_Elahi" title="Hasan Elahi" class="mw-redirect">Hasan Elahi</a> and run by distinguished faculty and <a href="/wiki/Graduate" title="Graduate">graduate</a> students. DCC students are housed in Queen Annes Hall and take a 16 credit, 2 year interdisciplinary curriculum centered on digital culture and innovative thinking in the digital world.<sup id="cite_ref-32" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-32"><span>[</span>32<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>Entrepreneurship and Innovation Program (EIP) is a living and learning honors program for Honors College freshmen and sophomores with an interdisciplinary, living and learning education to help build the entrepreneurial mindsets, skill sets, and relationships invaluable to developing innovative, impactful solutions to today's problems.<sup id="cite_ref-33" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-33"><span>[</span>33<span>]</span></a></sup> Through experiential learning, dynamic courses, seminars, workshops, competitions, and volunteerism, students receive a world-class education in entrepreneurship and innovation. In collaboration with faculty and mentors who have successfully launched new ventures, all student teams develop an innovative idea and write a product plan.<sup id="cite_ref-34" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-34"><span>[</span>34<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>Honors Humanities is the University of Maryland?s honors program for talented beginning undergraduates with interests in the humanities and creative arts. The selective two-year living-learning program combines a small <a href="/wiki/Liberal_arts_college" title="Liberal arts college">liberal arts college</a> environment with the dynamic resources of a large <a href="/wiki/Research_university" title="Research university" class="mw-redirect">research university</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-35" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-35"><span>[</span>35<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>The Gemstone Program at the University of Maryland is a multidisciplinary four-year research program for select undergraduate honors students of all majors. Under guidance of faculty mentors and Gemstone staff, teams of students design, direct and conduct research, often but not exclusively exploring the interdependence of science and technology with society.<sup id="cite_ref-36" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-36"><span>[</span>36<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>The Integrated Life Sciences (ILS) Program at the University of Maryland seeks to engage and inspire honors students interested in all aspects of biological research and biomedicine. The College of Computer, Mathematical, and Natural Sciences has partnered with the Honors College to create the ILS program, which offers nationally recognized innovations in the multidisciplinary training of life science and pre-medical students. The overall objective of the ILS experience is to prepare students for future successes in the most challenging programs in graduate, medical, dental, or other professional schools.<sup id="cite_ref-37" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-37"><span>[</span>37<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>University Honors is the largest living-learning program in the Honors College and allows students the greatest independence in shaping their education. University Honors welcomes students into a close-knit community of the University?s top faculty and intellectually gifted undergraduates committed to acquiring a broad and balanced education.<sup id="cite_ref-38" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-38"><span>[</span>38<span>]</span></a></sup> Students choose from over 130 engaging seminars exploring interdisciplinary topics in three broad areas: Contemporary Issues and Challenges, Arts and Sciences in Today's World, and Using the World as a Classroom.<sup id="cite_ref-39" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-39"><span>[</span>39<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>The <a href="/wiki/College_Park_Scholars" title="College Park Scholars">College Park Scholars</a> programs are two-year living-learning programs for first- and second-year students. Students are selected to enroll in one of 12 thematic programs: Arts; Business, Society, and the Economy; Environment, Technology, and Economy; Global Public Health; International Studies; Life Sciences; Media, Self, and Society; Public Leadership; Science and Global Change; Science, Discovery, and the Universe; Science, Technology, and Society. Students live together in dorms located in the Cambridge Community on North Campus.<sup id="cite_ref-40" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-40"><span>[</span>40<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <div class="thumb tright"> 
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a href="/wiki/File:UMD_mall_view.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/65/UMD_mall_view.JPG/220px-UMD_mall_view.JPG" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/65/UMD_mall_view.JPG/330px-UMD_mall_view.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/65/UMD_mall_view.JPG/440px-UMD_mall_view.JPG 2x" /></a> 
       <div class="thumbcaption"> 
        <div class="magnify">
         <a href="/wiki/File:UMD_mall_view.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"><img src="//bits.wikimedia.org/static-1.22wmf9/skins/common/images/magnify-clip.png" width="15" height="11" alt="" /></a>
        </div> A student working on 
        <a href="/wiki/McKeldin_Mall" title="McKeldin Mall">McKeldin Mall</a>.
       </div> 
      </div> 
     </div> 
     <p>The nation's first living-learning entrepreneurship program, <i><a href="/wiki/Brian_Hinman" title="Brian Hinman">Hinman</a> CEOs</i>, is geared toward students who are interested in starting their own business.<sup id="cite_ref-41" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-41"><span>[</span>41<span>]</span></a></sup> Students from all academic disciplines live together and are provided the resources to explore new business ventures.</p> 
     <p>The <a href="/wiki/QUEST_Honors_Fellows_Program" title="QUEST Honors Fellows Program">QUEST (Quality Enhancement Systems and Teams) Honors Fellows Program</a> engages undergraduate students from business, engineering, and computer, mathematical, and physical sciences. QUEST Students participate in courses focused on cross-functional collaboration, innovation, quality management, and teamwork.<sup id="cite_ref-42" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-42"><span>[</span>42<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>Other living-learning programs include: <a href="/wiki/University_of_Maryland_College_of_Behavioral_and_Social_Sciences#CIVICUS" title="University of Maryland College of Behavioral and Social Sciences">CIVICUS</a>, a two-year program in the <a href="/wiki/University_of_Maryland_College_of_Behavioral_and_Social_Sciences" title="University of Maryland College of Behavioral and Social Sciences">College of Behavioral and Social Sciences</a> based on the five principles of civil society;<sup id="cite_ref-43" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-43"><span>[</span>43<span>]</span></a></sup> Global Communities, a program that immerses students in a diverse culture (students from all over the world live in a community),<sup id="cite_ref-44" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-44"><span>[</span>44<span>]</span></a></sup> and the Language House,<sup id="cite_ref-45" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-45"><span>[</span>45<span>]</span></a></sup> which allows students pursuing language courses to live and practice with other students learning the same language.</p> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Faculty">Faculty</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_Maryland,_College_Park&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Faculty">edit</a>]</span></h3> 
     <div class="rellink relarticle mainarticle">
      Main article: 
      <a href="/wiki/List_of_University_of_Maryland,_College_Park_faculty" title="List of University of Maryland, College Park faculty" class="mw-redirect">List of University of Maryland, College Park faculty</a>
     </div> 
     <p>The university's faculty has included four Nobel Prize laureates. The earliest recipient, <a href="/wiki/Juan_Ram%C3%B3n_Jim%C3%A9nez" title="Juan Ram&oacute;n Jim&eacute;nez">Juan Ram&oacute;n Jim&eacute;nez</a>, was a professor of Spanish language and literature and won the 1956 prize for literature. Four decades later, physics professor <a href="/wiki/William_Daniel_Phillips" title="William Daniel Phillips">William Daniel Phillips</a> won the prize in physics for his contributions to <a href="/wiki/Laser_cooling" title="Laser cooling">laser cooling</a>, a technique to slow the movement of gaseous atoms in 1997. In 2005, professor emeritus of economics and public policy <a href="/wiki/Thomas_Schelling" title="Thomas Schelling">Thomas Schelling</a> was awarded the prize in economics for his contributions to <a href="/wiki/Game_theory" title="Game theory">game theory</a>. In 2006, adjunct professor of physics and senior astrophysicist at <a href="/wiki/NASA" title="NASA">NASA</a> <a href="/wiki/John_C._Mather" title="John C. Mather">John C. Mather</a> was awarded the prize in physics alongside <a href="/wiki/George_Smoot" title="George Smoot">George Smoot</a> for their work in the discovery of blackbody form and <a href="/wiki/Anisotropy" title="Anisotropy">anisotropy</a> of the <a href="/wiki/Cosmic_microwave_background_radiation" title="Cosmic microwave background radiation">cosmic microwave background radiation</a>. In addition, two University of Maryland alumni are Nobel Prize laureates; <a href="/wiki/Herbert_Hauptman" title="Herbert Hauptman" class="mw-redirect">Herbert Hauptman</a> won the 1985 prize in chemistry and <a href="/wiki/Raymond_Davis_Jr." title="Raymond Davis Jr." class="mw-redirect">Raymond Davis Jr.</a> won the 2002 prize in physics.</p> 
     <p>The University also has many notable academics in other fields of science. Professor of mathematics <a href="/wiki/Sergei_Novikov_(mathematician)" title="Sergei Novikov (mathematician)">Sergei Novikov</a> won the <a href="/wiki/Fields_Medal" title="Fields Medal">Fields Medal</a> in 1970 followed by alumnus <a href="/wiki/Charles_Fefferman" title="Charles Fefferman">Charles Fefferman</a> in 1978. Alumnus <a href="/wiki/George_Dantzig" title="George Dantzig">George Dantzig</a> won the 1975 <a href="/wiki/National_Medal_of_Science" title="National Medal of Science">National Medal of Science</a> for his work in the field of linear programming. Professor of physics <a href="/wiki/Michael_Fisher" title="Michael Fisher">Michael Fisher</a> won the <a href="/wiki/Wolf_Prize" title="Wolf Prize">Wolf Prize</a> in 1980 (together with <a href="/wiki/Kenneth_G._Wilson" title="Kenneth G. Wilson">Kenneth G. Wilson</a> and <a href="/wiki/Leo_Kadanoff" title="Leo Kadanoff">Leo Kadanoff</a>) and the <a href="/wiki/IUPAP" title="IUPAP" class="mw-redirect">IUPAP</a> <a href="/wiki/Boltzmann_Medal" title="Boltzmann Medal">Boltzmann Medal</a> in 1983. <a href="/wiki/James_A._Yorke" title="James A. Yorke">James A. Yorke</a>, a Distinguished University Professor of Mathematics and Physics and chair of the Mathematics Department won the 2003 <a href="/wiki/Japan_Prize" title="Japan Prize">Japan Prize</a> for his work in <a href="/wiki/Chaotic_systems" title="Chaotic systems" class="mw-redirect">chaotic systems</a>.</p> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Research">Research</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_Maryland,_College_Park&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Research">edit</a>]</span></h3> 
     <p>On October 14, 2004, the university added 150 acres (61&nbsp;ha) in an attempt to create the largest research park inside the Washington, D.C., <a href="/wiki/Interstate_495_(Capital_Beltway)" title="Interstate 495 (Capital Beltway)">Capital Beltway</a>, known as &quot;M Square.&quot;<sup id="cite_ref-46" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-46"><span>[</span>46<span>]</span></a></sup> The university completed construction on a new Bioscience Research Building on campus in May 2007. The <a href="/wiki/National_Oceanic_and_Atmospheric_Administration" title="National Oceanic and Atmospheric Administration">National Oceanic and Atmospheric Administration</a> (NOAA) is presently constructing the new <a href="/wiki/National_Centers_for_Environmental_Prediction" title="National Centers for Environmental Prediction">National Center for Weather and Climate Prediction</a> on site in M Square. It is scheduled to be completed in early 2009. The University's Physics Department constructed, operates, and maintains the world's largest isochronous synchrocyclotron.</p> 
     <div class="thumb tright"> 
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a href="/wiki/File:Glenn_L._Martin_Institute_of_Technology_at_UMCP,_2007.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/aa/Glenn_L._Martin_Institute_of_Technology_at_UMCP%2C_2007.jpg/220px-Glenn_L._Martin_Institute_of_Technology_at_UMCP%2C_2007.jpg" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/aa/Glenn_L._Martin_Institute_of_Technology_at_UMCP%2C_2007.jpg/330px-Glenn_L._Martin_Institute_of_Technology_at_UMCP%2C_2007.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/aa/Glenn_L._Martin_Institute_of_Technology_at_UMCP%2C_2007.jpg/440px-Glenn_L._Martin_Institute_of_Technology_at_UMCP%2C_2007.jpg 2x" /></a> 
       <div class="thumbcaption"> 
        <div class="magnify">
         <a href="/wiki/File:Glenn_L._Martin_Institute_of_Technology_at_UMCP,_2007.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"><img src="//bits.wikimedia.org/static-1.22wmf9/skins/common/images/magnify-clip.png" width="15" height="11" alt="" /></a>
        </div> Glenn L. Martin Institute of Technology
       </div> 
      </div> 
     </div> 
     <p>The University of Maryland's location near Washington, D.C. has created strong research partnerships, especially with government agencies. Many of the faculty members have funding from federal agencies such as the <a href="/wiki/National_Science_Foundation" title="National Science Foundation">National Science Foundation</a>, the <a href="/wiki/National_Institutes_of_Health" title="National Institutes of Health">National Institutes of Health</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-47" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-47"><span>[</span>47<span>]</span></a></sup> <a href="/wiki/National_Aeronautics_and_Space_Administration" title="National Aeronautics and Space Administration" class="mw-redirect">NASA</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-48" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-48"><span>[</span>48<span>]</span></a></sup> the <a href="/wiki/United_States_Department_of_Homeland_Security" title="United States Department of Homeland Security">Department of Homeland Security</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-49" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-49"><span>[</span>49<span>]</span></a></sup> the <a href="/wiki/National_Institute_of_Standards_and_Technology" title="National Institute of Standards and Technology">National Institute of Standards and Technology</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/National_Security_Agency" title="National Security Agency">National Security Agency</a>. These relationships have created numerous research opportunities for the university including: *taking the lead in the nationwide research initiative into the transmission and prevention of human and <a href="/wiki/Avian_influenza" title="Avian influenza">avian influenza</a><sup id="cite_ref-50" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-50"><span>[</span>50<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <ul> 
      <li>creating a new research center to study the behavioral and social foundations of terrorism with funding from the U.S. <a href="/wiki/Department_of_Homeland_Security" title="Department of Homeland Security" class="mw-redirect">Department of Homeland Security</a></li> 
      <li>launching the joint <a href="/wiki/NASA" title="NASA">NASA</a>-University of Maryland <i><a href="/wiki/Deep_Impact_(spacecraft)" title="Deep Impact (spacecraft)">Deep Impact</a></i> spacecraft in early January 2005.</li> 
     </ul> 
     <div class="thumb tleft"> 
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;">
       <a href="/wiki/File:UMD_Hornbake_Library.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/84/UMD_Hornbake_Library.JPG/170px-UMD_Hornbake_Library.JPG" width="170" height="227" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/84/UMD_Hornbake_Library.JPG/255px-UMD_Hornbake_Library.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/84/UMD_Hornbake_Library.JPG/340px-UMD_Hornbake_Library.JPG 2x" /></a> 
       <div class="thumbcaption"> 
        <div class="magnify">
         <a href="/wiki/File:UMD_Hornbake_Library.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"><img src="//bits.wikimedia.org/static-1.22wmf9/skins/common/images/magnify-clip.png" width="15" height="11" alt="" /></a>
        </div> 
        <a href="/wiki/Hornbake_Library" title="Hornbake Library" class="mw-redirect">Hornbake Library</a>
       </div> 
      </div> 
     </div> 
     <p>The <a href="/wiki/University_of_Maryland_Libraries" title="University of Maryland Libraries">University of Maryland Libraries</a> provide access to and assistance in the use of the scholarly information resources required to meet the education, research and service missions of the University.</p> 
     <p>The <a href="/wiki/Center_for_American_Politics_and_Citizenship" title="Center for American Politics and Citizenship">Center for American Politics and Citizenship</a> provides citizens and policy-makers with research on critical issues related to the United States' political institutions, processes, and policies. CAPC is a non-partisan, non-profit research institution within the Department of Government and Politics in the College of Behavioral and Social Sciences.</p> 
     <p>The <a href="/wiki/Space_Systems_Laboratory" title="Space Systems Laboratory">Space Systems Laboratory</a> researches human-robotic interaction for <a href="/wiki/Astronautics" title="Astronautics">astronautics</a> applications, and includes the only <a href="/wiki/Neutral_buoyancy" title="Neutral buoyancy">neutral buoyancy</a> facility at a university.</p> 
     <p>The <a href="/wiki/Center_for_Technology_and_Systems_Management" title="Center for Technology and Systems Management">Center for Technology and Systems Management</a> (<a href="/w/index.php?title=CTSM&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="CTSM (page does not exist)">CTSM</a>) has the mission to advance the state of the art of technology and systems analysis for the benefit of people and the environment. The focus has been always on enhancing safety, efficiency and effectiveness by performing reliability, risk, uncertainty or decision analysis studies.</p> 
     <p>The <a href="/wiki/Joint_Global_Change_Research_Institute" title="Joint Global Change Research Institute">Joint Global Change Research Institute</a> was formed in 2001 by the University of Maryland and the <a href="/wiki/Pacific_Northwest_National_Laboratory" title="Pacific Northwest National Laboratory">Pacific Northwest National Laboratory</a>. The institute focuses on multidisciplinary approaches of climate change research.</p> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Admissions">Admissions</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_Maryland,_College_Park&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Admissions">edit</a>]</span></h3> 
     <p>Admittance to the University of Maryland has become highly selective. According to the 2011 <a href="/wiki/US_News_and_World_Report" title="US News and World Report" class="mw-redirect">US News and World Report</a>, Maryland is rated &quot;Most Selective&quot; with a 41.9 percent acceptance rate.<sup id="cite_ref-51" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-51"><span>[</span>51<span>]</span></a></sup> The university regularly receives about 26,000 applications a year for a freshman class of 4,000, along with 6,500 transfer applications for 2,000 available transfer spots.<sup id="cite_ref-52" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-52"><span>[</span>52<span>]</span></a></sup> The incoming class for 2012 has a middle 50% SAT of 1250?1400 and average GPA of 4.11.<sup id="cite_ref-53" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-53"><span>[</span>53<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Rankings">Rankings</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_Maryland,_College_Park&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Rankings">edit</a>]</span></h3>

     <p>The University is ranked 58th in the latest 2012 <i><a href="/wiki/U.S._News_and_World_Report" title="U.S. News and World Report" class="mw-redirect">U.S. News and World Report</a></i> rankings of &quot;National Universities&quot; across the United States, and it is ranked 17th nationally among public universities. 29 undergraduate and graduate programs are ranked in the top 10 and 90 programs are in the top 25.<sup id="cite_ref-61" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-61"><span>[</span>61<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>The <a href="/wiki/Academic_Ranking_of_World_Universities" title="Academic Ranking of World Universities">Academic Ranking of World Universities</a> compiled by the <a href="/wiki/Shanghai_Jiao_Tong_University" title="Shanghai Jiao Tong University">Shanghai Jiao Tong University</a> ranked Maryland as 38th in the world as well as 8th among public flagship universities in the United States.<sup id="cite_ref-62" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-62"><span>[</span>62<span>]</span></a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Newsweek" title="Newsweek">Newsweek</a> ranked the University of Maryland as 45th in their ranking &quot;global universities.&quot; The <a href="/wiki/THE-QS_World_University_Rankings" title="THE-QS World University Rankings" class="mw-redirect">THE-QS World University Rankings</a> ranked the University of Maryland 104 on its top 400 universities in the world in 2010.<sup id="cite_ref-63" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-63"><span>[</span>63<span>]</span></a></sup> In 2011, <a href="/wiki/QS_World_University_Rankings" title="QS World University Rankings">QS World University Rankings</a><sup id="cite_ref-64" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-64"><span>[</span>64<span>]</span></a></sup> ranked the university 113th overall in the world.</p> 
     <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Campus">Campus</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_Maryland,_College_Park&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Campus">edit</a>]</span></h2> 
     <div class="thumb tright"> 
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;">
