     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Description">Description</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_Maryland,_College_Park&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Description">edit</a>]</span></h3> 
     <p>The campus of University of Maryland is noted for its red-brick <a href="/wiki/Georgian_architecture" title="Georgian architecture">Georgian</a> buildings and its large central lawn, named <a href="/wiki/McKeldin_Mall" title="McKeldin Mall">McKeldin Mall</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-65" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-65"><span>[</span>65<span>]</span></a></sup> White <a href="/wiki/Columns" title="Columns" class="mw-redirect">columns</a> decorate many <a href="/wiki/University_of_Maryland,_College_Park_Campus_Buildings" title="University of Maryland, College Park Campus Buildings">buildings</a>, with around 770 columns existing on campus.<sup id="cite_ref-66" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-66"><span>[</span>66<span>]</span></a></sup> Spanning the university's 1,250 acres (5.1&nbsp;km<sup>2</sup>) are over 7,500 documented trees and special garden plantings, leading the <a href="/wiki/American_Public_Gardens_Association" title="American Public Gardens Association">American Public Gardens Association</a> to designate the campus the <a href="/wiki/University_of_Maryland_Arboretum_%26_Botanical_Garden" title="University of Maryland Arboretum &amp; Botanical Garden">University of Maryland Arboretum &amp; Botanical Garden</a> in 2008.<sup id="cite_ref-universityvisitorsnetwork1_67-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-universityvisitorsnetwork1-67"><span>[</span>67<span>]</span></a></sup> This designation has allowed the university to showcase interesting species and specific gardens, including extensive native plantings. There are multiple arboretum tours, such as the centralized Tree Walking Tour which is based around McKeldin Mall and features 56 specimen trees.</p> 
     <p>Additionally, there are nearly 400 acres (1.6&nbsp;km<sup>2</sup>) of <a href="/wiki/Urban_forest" title="Urban forest">urban forest</a> located on campus<sup id="cite_ref-universityvisitorsnetwork1_67-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-universityvisitorsnetwork1-67"><span>[</span>67<span>]</span></a></sup> and the <a href="/wiki/National_Arbor_Day_Foundation" title="National Arbor Day Foundation">National Arbor Day Foundation</a> has named the university to its 'Tree Campus USA' list.<sup id="cite_ref-68" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-68"><span>[</span>68<span>]</span></a></sup> The recreational Paint Branch Trail, part of the <a href="/wiki/Anacostia_Tributary_Trails" title="Anacostia Tributary Trails" class="mw-redirect">Anacostia Tributary Trails</a> system, cuts through campus, as does the <a href="/wiki/Paint_Branch" title="Paint Branch">Paint Branch</a> stream, a tributary of the <a href="/wiki/Northeast_Branch_Anacostia_River" title="Northeast Branch Anacostia River">Northeast Branch Anacostia River</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-69" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-69"><span>[</span>69<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>McKeldin Mall serves as the center of campus. On the east and west ends of McKeldin Mall lie the Main Administration Building and <a href="/wiki/McKeldin_Library" title="McKeldin Library" class="mw-redirect">McKeldin Library</a>. Academic buildings surround McKeldin Mall on the north and south ends, and are the homes to many departments in the <a href="/wiki/University_of_Maryland_College_of_Behavioral_and_Social_Sciences" title="University of Maryland College of Behavioral and Social Sciences">College of Behavioral and Social Sciences</a>, College of Arts and Humanities, and the College of Agriculture and Natural Resources. West of McKeldin Mall is the North Hill Community, and south of McKeldin Mall lies <a href="/wiki/Morrill_Hall_(University_of_Maryland)" title="Morrill Hall (University of Maryland)">Morrill Hall</a> and the Morrill Quad, which was the original center of campus. South of the Morrill Quad are the South Hill and South Campus Commons Communities, and to the southwest is the Southwest Mall and the <a href="/wiki/Robert_H._Smith_School_of_Business" title="Robert H. Smith School of Business">Robert H. Smith School of Business</a>. Running parallel to McKeldin Mall to the north is Campus Drive, the main thoroughfare through campus. The <a href="/wiki/Adele_H._Stamp_Student_Union" title="Adele H. Stamp Student Union">Adele H. Stamp Student Union</a> sits along Campus Drive near the center of campus, and serves as a <a href="/wiki/Transit_center" title="Transit center" class="mw-redirect">transit center</a> for campus, where <a href="/wiki/Shuttle-UM" title="Shuttle-UM">Shuttle-UM</a> (the university's bus service) and municipal buses pick up and drop off passengers. Hornbake Plaza home to <a href="/wiki/Hornbake_Library" title="Hornbake Library" class="mw-redirect">Hornbake Library</a> and several buildings housing academic departments also lies on Campus Drive, east of Stamp.</p> 
     <div class="thumb tleft"> 
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a href="/wiki/File:UMD_Armory.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d9/UMD_Armory.JPG/220px-UMD_Armory.JPG" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d9/UMD_Armory.JPG/330px-UMD_Armory.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d9/UMD_Armory.JPG/440px-UMD_Armory.JPG 2x" /></a> 
       <div class="thumbcaption"> 
        <div class="magnify">
         <a href="/wiki/File:UMD_Armory.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"><img src="//bits.wikimedia.org/static-1.22wmf9/skins/common/images/magnify-clip.png" width="15" height="11" alt="" /></a>
        </div> The Armory.
       </div> 
      </div> 
     </div> 
     <div class="thumb tright"> 
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a href="/wiki/File:UMD_South_VCommons.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/UMD_South_VCommons.JPG/220px-UMD_South_VCommons.JPG" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/UMD_South_VCommons.JPG/330px-UMD_South_VCommons.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/UMD_South_VCommons.JPG/440px-UMD_South_VCommons.JPG 2x" /></a> 
       <div class="thumbcaption"> 
        <div class="magnify">
         <a href="/wiki/File:UMD_South_VCommons.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"><img src="//bits.wikimedia.org/static-1.22wmf9/skins/common/images/magnify-clip.png" width="15" height="11" alt="" /></a>
        </div> View near the South Commons residential area.
       </div> 
      </div> 
     </div> 
     <p>Outside of the Stamp Student Union on Campus Drive is the Jim Henson Statue and Memorial Garden, in honor of the late <a href="/wiki/Jim_Henson" title="Jim Henson">Jim Henson</a>, a Maryland alum. A likeness of Henson is seated on a park bench, facing arguably his most famous creation, <a href="/wiki/Kermit_the_frog" title="Kermit the frog" class="mw-redirect">Kermit the Frog</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-70" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-70"><span>[</span>70<span>]</span></a></sup> To the north and northwest of Stamp and Hornbake Plaza are the North Campus communities, <a href="/wiki/Byrd_Stadium" title="Byrd Stadium">Byrd Stadium</a>, the Eppley Recreation Center (the main gym on campus), the <a href="/wiki/Comcast_Center_(arena)" title="Comcast Center (arena)" class="mw-redirect">Comcast Center</a>, and the Wooded Hillock, a 22-acre (8.9&nbsp;ha) forest located next to the Comcast Center; Stadium Drive runs between the more southern Byrd Stadium and the rest of the these. The <a href="/wiki/Clarice_Smith_Performing_Arts_Center" title="Clarice Smith Performing Arts Center">Clarice Smith Performing Arts Center</a> sits to the west of Byrd Stadium. Another thoroughfare, Regents Drive, runs perpendicular to McKeldin Mall and is home to the iconic <a href="/wiki/Memorial_Chapel_(University_of_Maryland)" title="Memorial Chapel (University of Maryland)">Memorial Chapel</a> and the Campus Farms. Regents Drive crosses Campus Drive at the campus hallmark <a href="/wiki/%22M%22_Circle" title="&quot;M&quot; Circle">&quot;M&quot; Circle</a>, which is a traffic circle with a large &quot;M&quot; formed by flowers in its center.<sup id="cite_ref-71" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-71"><span>[</span>71<span>]</span></a></sup> The northeast quadrant of campus, formed by Campus and Regent Drives, is home to many of <a href="/wiki/Natural_sciences" title="Natural sciences" class="mw-redirect">natural sciences</a> and <a href="/wiki/Applied_sciences" title="Applied sciences" class="mw-redirect">applied sciences</a> departments. The university is also divided by <a href="/wiki/U.S._Route_1_in_Maryland" title="U.S. Route 1 in Maryland">U.S. Route 1</a>, known locally as &quot;Baltimore Avenue.&quot; While most of campus lies to the west of Baltimore Avenue, fixtures such as fraternity row and the Leonardtown Communities lie to the east. Sitting on the western edge of Baltimore Avenue are the Visitors' Center, also known as The Dairy, The Reckord Armory, and <a href="/wiki/The_Rossborough_Inn" title="The Rossborough Inn">The Rossborough Inn</a>, which, built during the years of 1798 to 1812, is the oldest building on campus (and is older than the university itself).<sup id="cite_ref-72" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-72"><span>[</span>72<span>]</span></a></sup> There are five regularly used entrances to campus; the main entrance, off of Baltimore Avenue and onto Campus Drive, is referred to as North Gate and features The Gatehouse, an ornate gateway honoring the university's founders.<sup id="cite_ref-73" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-73"><span>[</span>73<span>]</span></a></sup> The 140-acre (57&nbsp;ha), 18-hole <a href="/wiki/University_of_Maryland_Golf_Course" title="University of Maryland Golf Course">University of Maryland Golf Course</a> sits at the northern edge of campus, as does <a href="/wiki/University_of_Maryland_Observatory" title="University of Maryland Observatory">the Observatory</a>. The campus is also home to one of the <a href="/wiki/Root_nameserver" title="Root nameserver" class="mw-redirect">Root Servers</a>, responsible with operating DNS.</p> 
     <p>The campus is located 20 miles (32&nbsp;km) away from <a href="/wiki/Fort_Meade" title="Fort Meade" class="mw-redirect">Fort Meade</a> which houses the headquarters of the <a href="/wiki/National_Security_Agency" title="National Security Agency">National Security Agency</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-74" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-74"><span>[</span>74<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Sustainability">Sustainability</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_Maryland,_College_Park&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Sustainability">edit</a>]</span></h3> 
     <div class="thumb tright"> 
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a href="/wiki/File:UMD_McKeldin_sundial.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5e/UMD_McKeldin_sundial.JPG/220px-UMD_McKeldin_sundial.JPG" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5e/UMD_McKeldin_sundial.JPG/330px-UMD_McKeldin_sundial.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5e/UMD_McKeldin_sundial.JPG/440px-UMD_McKeldin_sundial.JPG 2x" /></a> 
       <div class="thumbcaption"> 
        <div class="magnify">
         <a href="/wiki/File:UMD_McKeldin_sundial.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"><img src="//bits.wikimedia.org/static-1.22wmf9/skins/common/images/magnify-clip.png" width="15" height="11" alt="" /></a>
        </div> The sundial in the center of 
        <a href="/wiki/McKeldin_Mall" title="McKeldin Mall">McKeldin Mall</a>, with 
        <a href="/wiki/McKeldin_Library" title="McKeldin Library" class="mw-redirect">McKeldin Library</a> in the background.
       </div> 
      </div> 
     </div> 
     <p>The four-person Office of Sustainability was created in summer 2007 after University President <a href="/wiki/Dan_Mote" title="Dan Mote" class="mw-redirect">Dan Mote</a> became charter signatory of the American College and Universities Presidents Climate Commitment (ACUPCC) with the goal of campus climate neutrality. The Climate Action Plan Work Group completed an inventory of campus emissions from 2002 to 2007, and finalized a Climate Action Plan in August 2009.<sup id="cite_ref-75" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-75"><span>[</span>75<span>]</span></a></sup> According to the university?s Climate Action Plan, Maryland aims to become carbon neutral by 2050.<sup id="cite_ref-76" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-76"><span>[</span>76<span>]</span></a></sup> All new constructions and major renovations must satisfy <a href="/wiki/Leed_Gold" title="Leed Gold" class="mw-redirect">LEED-Silver certification</a> requirements. The office has promoted several initiatives, including an increase in the recycling rate from 37% to a 54% recycling rate in 2008, due in part to the &quot;Feed the Turtle&quot; program for home football games.<sup id="cite_ref-UM_Sustainability_Snapshot_77-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-UM_Sustainability_Snapshot-77"><span>[</span>77<span>]</span></a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Power_Shift" title="Power Shift">Power Shift</a>, a national youth climate activism summit, was held at the University of Maryland in November 2007 with 6,000 individuals in attendance.<sup id="cite_ref-78" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-78"><span>[</span>78<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>The university's first <a href="/wiki/Leed_Gold" title="Leed Gold" class="mw-redirect">Leed Gold</a> building, Knight Hall, opened in April 2010 as the new home for the <a href="/wiki/Philip_Merrill_College_of_Journalism" title="Philip Merrill College of Journalism">Philip Merrill College of Journalism</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-79" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-79"><span>[</span>79<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-80" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-80"><span>[</span>80<span>]</span></a></sup> The university added <a href="/wiki/Solar_panels" title="Solar panels" class="mw-redirect">solar panels</a> in the spring of 2010 to the roof of &quot;The Diner&quot; dining hall in North Campus, and plans to add solar panels to the roof of <a href="/wiki/Cole_Field_House" title="Cole Field House">Cole Field House</a>, as well as additional campus buildings in the near future.<sup id="cite_ref-81" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-81"><span>[</span>81<span>]</span></a></sup> The university's announced 158,068-square-foot (14,685.0&nbsp;m<sup>2</sup>) state-of-the-art Physical Sciences Complex (set to be completed in July 2013) will meet <a href="/wiki/Leed_Gold" title="Leed Gold" class="mw-redirect">LEED-Silver certification</a> requirements.<sup id="cite_ref-82" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-82"><span>[</span>82<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-83" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-83"><span>[</span>83<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>In 2008, the Office of Sustainability started the Sustainability Advisors program, in which teachers invite a peer educator to give a lecture covering important sustainability concepts.<sup id="cite_ref-84" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-84"><span>[</span>84<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>The Office of Sustainability began an initiative called ?The Chesapeake Project? in 2009, in which professors integrate sustainability education into pre-existing classes across every discipline.<sup id="cite_ref-sustainability.umd.edu_85-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-sustainability.umd.edu-85"><span>[</span>85<span>]</span></a></sup> Participating professors must attend a two-day workshop in late May to learn about environmental, economic, and social sustainability.<sup id="cite_ref-sustainability.umd.edu_85-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-sustainability.umd.edu-85"><span>[</span>85<span>]</span></a></sup> All participants receive a $500 stipend. By the end of summer, workshop participants must submit a revised course plan for at least one course offered the following academic year. Since the inaugural workshop in 2009, 71 professors have participated in the program, implementing sustainability education into over 80 courses across all 12 colleges at the school.<sup id="cite_ref-sustainability.umd.edu_85-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-sustainability.umd.edu-85"><span>[</span>85<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>In 2011, Maryland?s team won the Solar Decathlon, a competition put on by the <a href="/wiki/U.S._Department_of_Energy" title="U.S. Department of Energy" class="mw-redirect">U.S. Department of Energy</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-solardecathlon.gov_86-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-solardecathlon.gov-86"><span>[</span>86<span>]</span></a></sup> The team designed and built a solar-powered home with a split butterfly roof in a project called ?WaterShed.&quot;<sup id="cite_ref-87" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-87"><span>[</span>87<span>]</span></a></sup> The house was ?inspired and guided by the Chesapeake Bay ecosystem, interconnecting the house with its landscape, and leading its dwellers toward a more sustainable lifestyle,? according to their <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://2011.solarteam.org/about">website</a>. Over 200 students contributed to the project. Maryland?s design beat out submissions from 20 other universities from all over the world, including China, New Zealand, Belgium, and Canada.<sup id="cite_ref-solardecathlon.gov_86-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-solardecathlon.gov-86"><span>[</span>86<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>On December 2, 2011 the University Senate approved the implementation of a sustainability minor.<sup id="cite_ref-88" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-88"><span>[</span>88<span>]</span></a></sup> Students could begin working towards the minor during the spring semester of that academic year, as the minor uses classes that are already offered. The minor is 15 credits.<sup id="cite_ref-89" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-89"><span>[</span>89<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>Maryland also promotes the use of reusable to-go containers at the dining hall, or OZZI containers, since the official launching of the program in August 2011<sup id="cite_ref-90" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-90"><span>[</span>90<span>]</span></a></sup> Students pay a $5 fee to initially use the container, but receive a coin when they return it to the dispenser. With the coin, the use of the container is cost-free.</p> 
     <p>In January 2011, Maryland installed occupancy sensors in nearly all of the 300 general-purpose classrooms.<sup id="cite_ref-diamondbackonline.com_91-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-diamondbackonline.com-91"><span>[</span>91<span>]</span></a></sup> These occupancy sensors automatically turn off the lights after 30 minutes if there is no motion in a room. The project is estimated to cut energy consumption by 30 percent and save the university $100,000 annually.<sup id="cite_ref-diamondbackonline.com_91-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-diamondbackonline.com-91"><span>[</span>91<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>In 2012, the University Sustainability fund granted $130,000 to projects that promote sustainability.<sup id="cite_ref-ReferenceA_92-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ReferenceA-92"><span>[</span>92<span>]</span></a></sup> The money was generated from an $8 mandatory sustainability fee, a fee that will increase to $12 by 2014. Mark Stewart, Project Manager at the Office of Sustainability, expects the fund to grow to $300,000 by 2013.<sup id="cite_ref-ReferenceA_92-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ReferenceA-92"><span>[</span>92<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>On May 2, 2012 the Wellness Coalition hosted its first Farmers Market at Maryland, a weekly tradition that supplies produce from farms in Maryland, Pennsylvania, and Virginia.<sup id="cite_ref-93" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-93"><span>[</span>93<span>]</span></a></sup> Its first day saw over 1,000 visitors.<sup id="cite_ref-94" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-94"><span>[</span>94<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Student_life">Student life</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_Maryland,_College_Park&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Student life">edit</a>]</span></h2> 
     <div class="rellink boilerplate seealso">
      See also: 
      <a href="/wiki/List_of_University_of_Maryland_student_organizations" title="List of University of Maryland student organizations">List of University of Maryland student organizations</a>
     </div> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Residential_life">Residential life</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_Maryland,_College_Park&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Residential life">edit</a>]</span></h3> 
     <div class="thumb tright"> 
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a href="/wiki/File:UMD_Talbot.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9b/UMD_Talbot.JPG/220px-UMD_Talbot.JPG" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9b/UMD_Talbot.JPG/330px-UMD_Talbot.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9b/UMD_Talbot.JPG/440px-UMD_Talbot.JPG 2x" /></a> 
       <div class="thumbcaption"> 
        <div class="magnify">
         <a href="/wiki/File:UMD_Talbot.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"><img src="//bits.wikimedia.org/static-1.22wmf9/skins/common/images/magnify-clip.png" width="15" height="11" alt="" /></a>
        </div> Talbot Hall in the South Hill community.
       </div> 
      </div> 
     </div> 
     <div class="thumb tright"> 
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a href="/wiki/File:UMD_brick_entryway.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4f/UMD_brick_entryway.JPG/220px-UMD_brick_entryway.JPG" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4f/UMD_brick_entryway.JPG/330px-UMD_brick_entryway.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4f/UMD_brick_entryway.JPG/440px-UMD_brick_entryway.JPG 2x" /></a> 
       <div class="thumbcaption"> 
        <div class="magnify">
         <a href="/wiki/File:UMD_brick_entryway.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"><img src="//bits.wikimedia.org/static-1.22wmf9/skins/common/images/magnify-clip.png" width="15" height="11" alt="" /></a>
        </div> Brick entryway near the South Hill Community.
       </div> 
      </div> 
     </div> 
     <p>There are two main residential areas on campus, North Campus and South Campus, which are further divided into a total of seven residential communities. North Campus is made up of Cambridge Community (which consists of five residence halls), Denton Community (which currently consists of four halls, including Oakland hall which opened in the fall semester of 2011), and Ellicott Community (consisting of three halls). South Campus includes the North Hill Community, made up of nine <a href="/wiki/Georgian-style" title="Georgian-style" class="mw-redirect">Georgian-style</a> halls located immediately west of <a href="/wiki/McKeldin_Mall" title="McKeldin Mall">McKeldin Mall</a>, South Hill Community, made up of fourteen small residence halls for upperclassmen, Leonardtown Community, which offers apartment-style living and is further divided into Old Leonardtown (consisting of six buildings) and New Leonardtown (also consisting of six buildings), the South Campus Commons Community, which consists of seven apartment-style buildings (the seventh and most recent building being opened in January 2010), and the Courtyards, a garden style apartment community in north campus consisting of seven buildings. The South Campus Commons Community and Courtyards, while built on campus, are managed by a private company, Capstone On-Campus Management, as part of a public-private partnership between the company and the University of Maryland.</p> 
     <p>The university does not have family housing. As of 2011 some students with families have advocated for the addition of family housing.<sup id="cite_ref-95" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-95"><span>[</span>95<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>Residential life is overseen by the Department of Resident Life, which consists of a hierarchical structure of staff members and many individual departments. For instance, <a href="/wiki/Resident_assistants" title="Resident assistants" class="mw-redirect">Resident assistants</a>, who are full-time undergraduates facilitating the student interaction and development of floors within their assigned floor, building, or community, are supervised by <a href="/w/index.php?title=Resident_directors&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Resident directors (page does not exist)">Resident directors</a>. The Department of Resident Life offers its residents and other students many programs, including the Math Success Program, Academic Success Program, Common Ground Dialogue Program, and many Living and Learning programs.<sup id="cite_ref-96" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-96"><span>[</span>96<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>For students living in the residence halls, the Department seeks to encourage a multicultural experience through its <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://www.resnet.umd.edu/aboutus/multicultural/">Multicultural Philosophy</a>. This philosophy emphasizes that all of the residents should feel that they belong to within residence hall and within the University of Maryland as a whole regardless of their diverse backgrounds (e.g. race, ethnicity, sexual orientation, religion, disability/ability, etc.).</p> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Dining">Dining</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_Maryland,_College_Park&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: Dining">edit</a>]</span></h3> 
     <p>There are two main dining halls on campus: The Diner is located in the Ellicott Community, and the South Campus Dining Room is located near the South Hill and South Campus Commons communities. Located in the Denton Community, 251 North is the third dining hall on campus and features the first all-you-can-eat style dining experience on campus. A <a href="/wiki/Adele_H._Stamp_Student_Union#Dining_Options" title="Adele H. Stamp Student Union">food court in the Stamp Student Union</a> provides a plethora of dining options for the university community. There are a wide array of fast-food chain restaurants that students can purchase food from using their Terp Bucks. The selection includes Sbarro Pizza, McDonald's, Moby Dick House of Kabob, Subway, Taco Bell, Chick-fil-A, Panda Express and a newly added (2012) Auntie Anne's Pretzels. Additionally, twelve caf&eacute;s are located throughout campus as are five convenience stores (known as &quot;shops&quot;). Two restaurants exists on campus: Adele's Restaurant in the <a href="/wiki/Stamp_Student_Union" title="Stamp Student Union" class="mw-redirect">Stamp Student Union</a> and Mulligan's Grill and Pub, located on the <a href="/wiki/University_of_Maryland_Golf_Course" title="University of Maryland Golf Course">University of Maryland Golf Course</a>.</p> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Transportation">Transportation</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_Maryland,_College_Park&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: Transportation">edit</a>]</span></h3> 
     <div class="thumb tleft"> 
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a href="/wiki/File:College_Park-U_of_Md_Station.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0a/College_Park-U_of_Md_Station.jpg/220px-College_Park-U_of_Md_Station.jpg" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0a/College_Park-U_of_Md_Station.jpg/330px-College_Park-U_of_Md_Station.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0a/College_Park-U_of_Md_Station.jpg/440px-College_Park-U_of_Md_Station.jpg 2x" /></a> 
       <div class="thumbcaption"> 
        <div class="magnify">
         <a href="/wiki/File:College_Park-U_of_Md_Station.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"><img src="//bits.wikimedia.org/static-1.22wmf9/skins/common/images/magnify-clip.png" width="15" height="11" alt="" /></a>
        </div> 
        <a href="/wiki/College_Park-University_of_Maryland_(Washington_Metro)" title="College Park-University of Maryland (Washington Metro)" class="mw-redirect">College Park-University of Maryland</a> metro station provides easy and quick access to 
        <a href="/wiki/Downtown_Washington_DC" title="Downtown Washington DC" class="mw-redirect">Downtown Washington DC</a>.
       </div> 
      </div> 
     </div> 
     <p>The university is served by <a href="/wiki/Transportation_in_Washington,_D.C.#Air" title="Transportation in Washington, D.C.">the three airports</a> which exist in the greater <a href="/wiki/Washington_metropolitan_area" title="Washington metropolitan area">Washington metropolitan area</a>. A small public airport in College Park, <a href="/wiki/College_Park_Airport" title="College Park Airport">College Park Airport</a>, lies nearly adjacent to campus, but operations are limited.</p> 
     <p>A free shuttle service, known as <a href="/wiki/Shuttle-UM" title="Shuttle-UM">Shuttle-UM</a>, is available for all UMD students, faculty, and staff. The university is served by an off-campus stop on the <a href="/wiki/Washington_DC_Metro" title="Washington DC Metro" class="mw-redirect">Washington DC Metro</a> <a href="/wiki/Green_Line_(Washington_Metro)" title="Green Line (Washington Metro)">Green Line</a> called <a href="/wiki/College_Park_%E2%80%93_University_of_Maryland_(Washington_Metro)" title="College Park ? University of Maryland (Washington Metro)" class="mw-redirect">College Park ? University of Maryland</a>. The station is also served by the <a href="/wiki/Camden_Line" title="Camden Line">Camden Line</a> of the <a href="/wiki/MARC_train" title="MARC train" class="mw-redirect">MARC train</a>, which runs between <a href="/wiki/Baltimore" title="Baltimore">Baltimore</a> and <a href="/wiki/Washington_DC" title="Washington DC" class="mw-redirect">Washington</a>. A Shuttle-UM bus (Route 104) arrives at the metro station every five minutes during fall and spring semesters (every ten minutes during the summer) to bring all visitors to campus (currently stopping in front of the <a href="/wiki/Stamp_Student_Union" title="Stamp Student Union" class="mw-redirect">Stamp Student Union</a>). The <a href="/wiki/DC_Metrobus" title="DC Metrobus" class="mw-redirect">DC Metrobus</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Prince_George%27s_County" title="Prince George's County" class="mw-redirect">Prince George's County</a> <a href="/wiki/TheBus_(Prince_George%27s_County)" title="TheBus (Prince George's County)">TheBus</a> bus services also stop on campus. There is an additional service called <a href="/w/index.php?title=Nite_Ride&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Nite Ride (page does not exist)">Nite Ride</a> which is a curb-to-curb service offered every night from 5:30&nbsp;pm to 7:30&nbsp;am. This service is designed to serve the areas of campus that are not included on the evening service routes.</p> 
     <p>In addition, beginning in early 2012, <a href="/wiki/Prince_George%27s_County" title="Prince George's County" class="mw-redirect">Prince George's County</a> <a href="/wiki/TheBus_(Prince_George%27s_County)" title="TheBus (Prince George's County)">TheBus</a> bus services were made free of charge to all University of Maryland Students and Staff.<sup id="cite_ref-97" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-97"><span>[</span>97<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>Over 21,000 parking spaces are on campus, in numerous parking lots and garages.<sup id="cite_ref-autogenerated1_98-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-autogenerated1-98"><span>[</span>98<span>]</span></a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Zipcar" title="Zipcar">Zipcar</a> service is also available on campus for all UMD students, faculty, and staff.<sup id="cite_ref-99" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-99"><span>[</span>99<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>The university has been attempting to make the campus more bike-friendly by installing covered bike parking and bike lockers on campus,<sup id="cite_ref-100" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-100"><span>[</span>100<span>]</span></a></sup> introducing a bike-sharing program,<sup id="cite_ref-101" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-101"><span>[</span>101<span>]</span></a></sup> and plans to add more bike lanes on campus.<sup id="cite_ref-102" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-102"><span>[</span>102<span>]</span></a></sup> As of Spring 2011, the University has stayed committed to encouraging bicycling on campus by installing covered bike storage outside of the newly built Oakland dorm as well as security lockers in the Mowatt Lane Garage.<sup id="cite_ref-103" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-103"><span>[</span>103<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-104" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-104"><span>[</span>104<span>]</span></a></sup> In addition to increased storage options, the University runs the Campus Bike Shop where students can get their bikes repaired and learn how to maintain them on their own.<sup id="cite_ref-105" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-105"><span>[</span>105<span>]</span></a></sup> The installation of one or more <a href="/wiki/Light-rail" title="Light-rail" class="mw-redirect">light-rail</a> stops on campus as a part of metropolitan Washington's proposed <a href="/wiki/Purple_Line_(Maryland)" title="Purple Line (Maryland)">Purple Line</a> is an ongoing debate.<sup id="cite_ref-106" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-106"><span>[</span>106<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-107" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-107"><span>[</span>107<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="The_Diamondback"><i>The Diamondback</i></span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_Maryland,_College_Park&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: The Diamondback">edit</a>]</span></h3> 
     <div class="rellink relarticle mainarticle">
      Main article: 
      <a href="/wiki/The_Diamondback" title="The Diamondback">The Diamondback</a>
     </div> 
     <div class="thumb tright"> 
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a href="/wiki/File:UMD_Stamp_co-op,_food_court_beams.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b7/UMD_Stamp_co-op%2C_food_court_beams.jpg/220px-UMD_Stamp_co-op%2C_food_court_beams.jpg" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b7/UMD_Stamp_co-op%2C_food_court_beams.jpg/330px-UMD_Stamp_co-op%2C_food_court_beams.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b7/UMD_Stamp_co-op%2C_food_court_beams.jpg/440px-UMD_Stamp_co-op%2C_food_court_beams.jpg 2x" /></a> 
       <div class="thumbcaption"> 
        <div class="magnify">
         <a href="/wiki/File:UMD_Stamp_co-op,_food_court_beams.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"><img src="//bits.wikimedia.org/static-1.22wmf9/skins/common/images/magnify-clip.png" width="15" height="11" alt="" /></a>
        </div> Atrium of 
        <a href="/wiki/Stamp_Student_Union" title="Stamp Student Union" class="mw-redirect">Stamp Student Union</a>, near the food court and co-op
       </div> 
      </div> 
     </div> 
     <p><i>The Diamondback</i> is the independent <a href="/wiki/Student_newspaper" title="Student newspaper">student newspaper</a> of the University of Maryland. It was founded in 1910 as <i>The Triangle</i> and renamed in 1921 in honor of a local reptile, the <a href="/wiki/Diamondback_terrapin" title="Diamondback terrapin">Diamondback terrapin</a>, which became the official school mascot in 1933. The newspaper is published daily Monday through Friday during the Spring and Fall semesters, with a print circulation of 17,000 and annual advertising revenues of over $1 million.<sup id="cite_ref-108" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-108"><span>[</span>108<span>]</span></a></sup> It has four sections: News, Opinion, Sports, and Diversions.</p> 
     <p>For the 2008?2009 school year, &quot;The Diamondback&quot; earned a Mark of Excellence award from the <a href="/wiki/Society_of_Professional_Journalists" title="Society of Professional Journalists">Society of Professional Journalists</a>, placing second nationally for Best All-Around Daily Student Newspaper and first in its region in the same category.<sup id="cite_ref-109" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-109"><span>[</span>109<span>]</span></a></sup> Three years earlier the newspaper had finished <a href="/w/index.php?title=Third_place_nationally&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Third place nationally (page does not exist)">third place nationally</a> for Best All-Around Daily Student Newspaper and first in its region.<sup id="cite_ref-110" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-110"><span>[</span>110<span>]</span></a></sup> Notable journalists who have been with <i>The Diamondback</i> include <a href="/wiki/David_Simon_(writer)" title="David Simon (writer)" class="mw-redirect">David Simon</a> of HBO's <i>The Wire</i> and NBC's <i>Homicide: Life on the Street</i>, disgraced <a href="/wiki/Jayson_Blair" title="Jayson Blair">Jayson Blair</a>, who was editor-in-chief in 1996 (Blair did not graduate, instead taking a job with <a href="/wiki/The_New_York_Times" title="The New York Times">The New York Times</a>); <a href="/wiki/Norman_Chad" title="Norman Chad">Norman Chad</a>, who was editor-in-chief in 1978; cartoonists <a href="/wiki/Jeff_Kinney_(writer)" title="Jeff Kinney (writer)">Jeff Kinney</a>, who created the <i><a href="/wiki/Diary_of_a_Wimpy_Kid" title="Diary of a Wimpy Kid">Diary of a Wimpy Kid</a></i> fiction series and whose <i>Igdoof</i> strip appeared in <i>The Diamondback</i>; <a href="/wiki/Aaron_McGruder" title="Aaron McGruder">Aaron McGruder</a>, who first published his cartoon <i><a href="/wiki/The_Boondocks_(TV_series)" title="The Boondocks (TV series)">The Boondocks</a></i> in <i>The Diamondback</i>; and <a href="/wiki/Frank_Cho" title="Frank Cho">Frank Cho</a>, who began his career with the popular &quot;University Squared&quot; for The Diamondback.</p> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="WMUC-FM">WMUC-FM</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_Maryland,_College_Park&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: WMUC-FM">edit</a>]</span></h3> 
     <div class="rellink relarticle mainarticle">
      Main article: 
      <a href="/wiki/WMUC-FM" title="WMUC-FM">WMUC-FM</a>
     </div> 
     <p>WMUC-FM (88.1 FM) is the university's non-commercial radio station, staffed entirely by UMD students and volunteers. WMUC is a <a href="/wiki/Freeform_radio" title="Freeform radio" class="mw-redirect">freeform radio</a> station that broadcasts at 10 watts. Its broadcasts can be heard throughout the <a href="/wiki/Washington_metropolitan_area" title="Washington metropolitan area">Washington metropolitan area</a>. Notable WMUC alumni include <a href="/wiki/Connie_Chung" title="Connie Chung">Connie Chung</a>, <a href="/wiki/Bonnie_Bernstein" title="Bonnie Bernstein">Bonnie Bernstein</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Aaron_McGruder" title="Aaron McGruder">Aaron McGruder</a>.</p> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Greek_life">Greek life</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_Maryland,_College_Park&amp;action=edit&amp;section=23" title="Edit section: Greek life">edit</a>]</span></h3> 
     <div class="thumb tright"> 
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a href="/wiki/File:UMCP_Administration_building,_seen_from_end_of_reflecting_pool_at_morning,_August_21,_2006.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cf/UMCP_Administration_building%2C_seen_from_end_of_reflecting_pool_at_morning%2C_August_21%2C_2006.jpg/220px-UMCP_Administration_building%2C_seen_from_end_of_reflecting_pool_at_morning%2C_August_21%2C_2006.jpg" width="220" height="166" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cf/UMCP_Administration_building%2C_seen_from_end_of_reflecting_pool_at_morning%2C_August_21%2C_2006.jpg/330px-UMCP_Administration_building%2C_seen_from_end_of_reflecting_pool_at_morning%2C_August_21%2C_2006.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cf/UMCP_Administration_building%2C_seen_from_end_of_reflecting_pool_at_morning%2C_August_21%2C_2006.jpg/440px-UMCP_Administration_building%2C_seen_from_end_of_reflecting_pool_at_morning%2C_August_21%2C_2006.jpg 2x" /></a> 
       <div class="thumbcaption"> 
        <div class="magnify">
         <a href="/wiki/File:UMCP_Administration_building,_seen_from_end_of_reflecting_pool_at_morning,_August_21,_2006.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"><img src="//bits.wikimedia.org/static-1.22wmf9/skins/common/images/magnify-clip.png" width="15" height="11" alt="" /></a>
        </div> Administration building, seen from end of reflecting pool.
       </div> 
      </div> 
     </div> 
     <p>About 14% of men and 17% of women in Maryland's undergraduate student body are involved in <a href="/wiki/Fraternities_and_sororities" title="Fraternities and sororities" class="mw-redirect">Greek life</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-111" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-111"><span>[</span>111<span>]</span></a></sup> Many of the fraternities and sororities at the school are located on Fraternity Row and the Graham Cracker, which are controlled by the University. Fraternity Row is the background of several <a href="/wiki/University_of_Maryland,_College_Park#Filmography" title="University of Maryland, College Park">recently produced films</a>.</p> 
     <p>All social Greek organizations are governed by one of three groups: the Inter-Fraternity Council, the Panhellenic Association, or the Pan-Hellenic Council. All cultural Greek organizations are governed by the United Greek Council. These councils assist in the creation and governance of chapter by-laws, risk management plans, and philanthropic activities, with support from the Department of Fraternity and Sorority Life.<sup id="cite_ref-112" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-112"><span>[</span>112<span>]</span></a></sup> Each year, every Greek organization must fulfill certain requirements, including doing a service and conducting a program/event related to community service, diversity, or alumni and faculty outreach.</p>

     <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Athletics">Athletics</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_Maryland,_College_Park&amp;action=edit&amp;section=24" title="Edit section: Athletics">edit</a>]</span></h2> 
     <div class="rellink relarticle mainarticle">
      Main article: 
      <a href="/wiki/Maryland_Terrapins" title="Maryland Terrapins">Maryland Terrapins</a>
     </div> 
     <div class="thumb tright"> 
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a href="/wiki/File:Comcast_Center_interior.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0c/Comcast_Center_interior.jpg/220px-Comcast_Center_interior.jpg" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0c/Comcast_Center_interior.jpg/330px-Comcast_Center_interior.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0c/Comcast_Center_interior.jpg/440px-Comcast_Center_interior.jpg 2x" /></a> 
       <div class="thumbcaption"> 
        <div class="magnify">
         <a href="/wiki/File:Comcast_Center_interior.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"><img src="//bits.wikimedia.org/static-1.22wmf9/skins/common/images/magnify-clip.png" width="15" height="11" alt="" /></a>
        </div> 
        <a href="/wiki/Comcast_Center_(arena)" title="Comcast Center (arena)" class="mw-redirect">Comcast Center</a>, home of Maryland basketball
       </div> 
      </div> 
     </div> 
     <p>The university sponsors varsity athletic teams in 17&nbsp;men's and women's sports. The teams, nicknamed the &quot;Terrapins&quot;, represent Maryland in <a href="/wiki/National_Collegiate_Athletic_Association" title="National Collegiate Athletic Association">National Collegiate Athletic Association</a> <a href="/wiki/Division_I_(NCAA)" title="Division I (NCAA)">Division I</a> competition. Maryland became a founding member of the <a href="/wiki/Atlantic_Coast_Conference" title="Atlantic Coast Conference">Atlantic Coast Conference</a> in 1952. As of December 2010, Maryland's athletic teams have been awarded 38&nbsp;national championships by the NCAA, <a href="/wiki/United_States_Intercollegiate_Lacrosse_Association" title="United States Intercollegiate Lacrosse Association">USILA</a>, <a href="/wiki/Association_for_Intercollegiate_Athletics_for_Women" title="Association for Intercollegiate Athletics for Women">AIAW</a>, and <a href="/wiki/National_Cheerleaders_Association" title="National Cheerleaders Association">NCA</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-113" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-113"><span>[</span>113<span>]</span></a></sup> In 2008 and 2010, <i><a href="/wiki/The_Princeton_Review" title="The Princeton Review">The Princeton Review</a></i> named the University of Maryland's athletic facilities the best in the nation.<sup id="cite_ref-114" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-114"><span>[</span>114<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-115" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-115"><span>[</span>115<span>]</span></a></sup> The Terrapins nickname (often shortened to &quot;Terps&quot;) was coined by former university president, football coach, and athletic director <a href="/wiki/Curly_Byrd" title="Curly Byrd" class="mw-redirect">H. C. &quot;Curly&quot; Byrd</a> in 1932.<sup id="cite_ref-116" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-116"><span>[</span>116<span>]</span></a></sup> The mascot is a <a href="/wiki/Diamondback_terrapin" title="Diamondback terrapin">diamondback terrapin</a> named <i>Testudo</i>, which is <a href="/wiki/Latin" title="Latin">Latin</a> for &quot;tortoise.&quot;<sup id="cite_ref-117" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-117"><span>[</span>117<span>]</span></a></sup> Since the early 20th century, the school athletic colors have been some combination of those on the <a href="/wiki/Flag_of_Maryland" title="Flag of Maryland">Maryland state flag</a>: red, white, black, and gold.<sup id="cite_ref-118" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-118"><span>[</span>118<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <div class="thumb tright"> 
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a href="/wiki/File:Chevy_Chase_Field_at_Byrd_Stadium_9-13-08.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9c/Chevy_Chase_Field_at_Byrd_Stadium_9-13-08.jpg/220px-Chevy_Chase_Field_at_Byrd_Stadium_9-13-08.jpg" width="220" height="96" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9c/Chevy_Chase_Field_at_Byrd_Stadium_9-13-08.jpg/330px-Chevy_Chase_Field_at_Byrd_Stadium_9-13-08.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9c/Chevy_Chase_Field_at_Byrd_Stadium_9-13-08.jpg/440px-Chevy_Chase_Field_at_Byrd_Stadium_9-13-08.jpg 2x" /></a> 
       <div class="thumbcaption"> 
        <div class="magnify">
         <a href="/wiki/File:Chevy_Chase_Field_at_Byrd_Stadium_9-13-08.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"><img src="//bits.wikimedia.org/static-1.22wmf9/skins/common/images/magnify-clip.png" width="15" height="11" alt="" /></a>
        </div> 
        <a href="/wiki/Byrd_Stadium" title="Byrd Stadium">Byrd Stadium</a> &quot;near capacity&quot; on game day
       </div> 
      </div> 
     </div> 
     <p><a href="/wiki/Maryland_Terrapins_men%27s_basketball" title="Maryland Terrapins men's basketball">Men's basketball</a> is one of the most popular sports at the university.<sup id="cite_ref-crawler_119-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-crawler-119"><span>[</span>119<span>]</span></a></sup> Long-time head coach <a href="/wiki/Lefty_Driesell" title="Lefty Driesell">Lefty Driesell</a> began the now nationwide tradition of &quot;<a href="/wiki/Midnight_Madness_(basketball)" title="Midnight Madness (basketball)">Midnight Madness</a> in 1971.<sup id="cite_ref-120" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-120"><span>[</span>120<span>]</span></a></sup> Beginning in 1989, alumnus <a href="/wiki/Gary_Williams" title="Gary Williams">Gary Williams</a> revived the program, which was struggling in the wake of <a href="/wiki/Len_Bias" title="Len Bias">Len Bias</a>'s death and NCAA rules infractions. Williams led Maryland basketball to national prominence with two <a href="/wiki/NCAA_Men%27s_Division_I_Basketball_Tournament" title="NCAA Men's Division I Basketball Tournament" class="mw-redirect">Final Four</a> appearances, and in 2002, a <a href="/wiki/2002_NCAA_Men%27s_Division_I_Basketball_Tournament" title="2002 NCAA Men's Division I Basketball Tournament">national championship</a>. On February 7, 2006, Gary Williams won his 349th game to surpass Driesell and became Maryland's all-time leader among basketball coaches. In May 2011 Williams retired allowing for the entrance of new head coach, Mark Turgeon. The court at Comcast Center at the UMD was named in honor of the dearly beloved coach, Gary Williams. <a href="/wiki/Maryland_Terrapins_football" title="Maryland Terrapins football">Maryland football</a> is also popular at the university.<sup id="cite_ref-crawler_119-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-crawler-119"><span>[</span>119<span>]</span></a></sup> The Terrapins were awarded the national championship by the wire services in 1953, and in 1951, by several retroactive selectors. Maryland has secured eleven conference championships, including nine in the ACC, which ranks third most in the league. The Terrapins most recently won the ACC in <a href="/wiki/2001_Maryland_Terrapins_football_team" title="2001 Maryland Terrapins football team">2001</a> under alumnus and head coach <a href="/wiki/Ralph_Friedgen" title="Ralph Friedgen">Ralph Friedgen</a>.</p> 
     <div class="thumb tright"> 
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a href="/wiki/File:D1_Lacrosse.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/24/D1_Lacrosse.jpg/220px-D1_Lacrosse.jpg" width="220" height="146" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/24/D1_Lacrosse.jpg/330px-D1_Lacrosse.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/24/D1_Lacrosse.jpg/440px-D1_Lacrosse.jpg 2x" /></a> 
       <div class="thumbcaption"> 
        <div class="magnify">
         <a href="/wiki/File:D1_Lacrosse.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"><img src="//bits.wikimedia.org/static-1.22wmf9/skins/common/images/magnify-clip.png" width="15" height="11" alt="" /></a>
        </div> 
        <a href="/wiki/Maryland_Terrapins_men%27s_lacrosse" title="Maryland Terrapins men's lacrosse">Maryland</a> fields one of the nation's premier 
        <a href="/wiki/Field_lacrosse" title="Field lacrosse">lacrosse</a> programs.
       </div> 
      </div> 
     </div> 
     <p>Beyond the two &quot;revenue sports,&quot; the university fields 15&nbsp;other varsity teams. <a href="/wiki/Maryland_Terrapins_men%27s_lacrosse" title="Maryland Terrapins men's lacrosse">Maryland men's lacrosse</a> remains one of the sport's top programs since its beginnings as a squad in 1865,<sup id="cite_ref-121" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-121"><span>[</span>121<span>]</span></a></sup> although it last won the national championship in <a href="/wiki/1975_NCAA_Division_I_Men%27s_Lacrosse_Championship" title="1975 NCAA Division I Men's Lacrosse Championship">1975</a>. The team has secured ten <a href="/wiki/United_States_Intercollegiate_Lacrosse_Association" title="United States Intercollegiate Lacrosse Association">USILA</a> and NCAA national championships since its promotion to varsity status in 1924, and is a regular fixture in the <a href="/wiki/NCAA_Division_I_Men%27s_Lacrosse_Championship" title="NCAA Division I Men's Lacrosse Championship" class="mw-redirect">NCAA tournament</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-122" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-122"><span>[</span>122<span>]</span></a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Maryland_Terrapins_women%27s_lacrosse" title="Maryland Terrapins women's lacrosse">women's lacrosse team</a> has the most national championships of any program in the nation, including most recently in 2010.<sup id="cite_ref-123" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-123"><span>[</span>123<span>]</span></a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Maryland_Terrapins_women%27s_basketball" title="Maryland Terrapins women's basketball">women's basketball team</a> rose to prominence in the 2000s (decade), and head coach <a href="/wiki/Brenda_Frese" title="Brenda Frese">Brenda Frese</a> guided the Lady Terps to their first NCAA title in 2006.<sup id="cite_ref-124" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-124"><span>[</span>124<span>]</span></a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Maryland_Terrapins_men%27s_soccer" title="Maryland Terrapins men's soccer">men' soccer team</a> has reached five Final Fours since 1997 under the guidance of head coach <a href="/wiki/Sasho_Cirovski" title="Sasho Cirovski">Sasho Cirovski</a>, and captured the <a href="/wiki/College_Cup" title="College Cup" class="mw-redirect">College Cup</a> in 2005 and 2008. The soccer team has developed a devoted and large fan base of both students and local community members. The rowdy group of students named, &quot;The Crew&quot; pride themselves on their dedication to the team and skills at distracting the opposing goalie. At Ludwig field, stands are secured behind each goal allowing The Crew to continuously mock and ridicule the opposing goalie the entire game. In 2008, the fan record at Ludwig field was set at 6,500 when MD took on ACC opponent, Wake Forest. Under the encouragement of The Crew and head coach, the total year attendance has increased dramatically since 1995. In 1995 the total attendance was 12, 710. By 2008, the yearly attendance was to 35, 631.<sup id="cite_ref-125" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-125"><span>[</span>125<span>]</span></a></sup> The women's <a href="/wiki/Field_hockey" title="Field hockey">field hockey</a> team has secured seven NCAA championships.<sup id="cite_ref-126" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-126"><span>[</span>126<span>]</span></a></sup> The Maryland <a href="/wiki/Collegiate_wrestling" title="Collegiate wrestling">wrestling</a> team was dominant in the ACC throughout the 1950s and 1960s and returned to claim two more conference titles in the late 2000s (decade).<sup id="cite_ref-127" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-127"><span>[</span>127<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>The <a href="/wiki/Mighty_Sound_of_Maryland" title="Mighty Sound of Maryland">Mighty Sound of Maryland</a> marching band attends all home football games and provides pre-game performances.<sup id="cite_ref-128" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-128"><span>[</span>128<span>]</span></a></sup> During the basketball season, the marching band becomes the University of Maryland Pep Band, which provides music in the stands at men's and women's home games and during tournament play.<sup id="cite_ref-129" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-129"><span>[</span>129<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>As a result of budget cuts, on November 21, 2011, University President Wallace Loh said he supported a committee's recommendation to cut funding for six of the athletic programs which would eliminate eight teams. However, the president did show support for &quot;Save the Programs Campaign&quot; which was a program giving teams a chance to raise 8 years of total program costs by June 30, 2012. If the funds were not raised, all eight teams would be cut on July 1, 2012. The affected teams were men's cross country, indoor track, and outdoor track, men's swimming and diving, men's tennis, women's acrobatics and tumbling, women's swimming and diving, and women's water polo. On July 1, 2012, the University officially cut 7 of those teams. The men?s outdoor track team needed to raise $940,000 and managed to raise $888,000, which was deemed close enough that it was not cut.<sup id="cite_ref-130" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-130"><span>[</span>130<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>On November 19, 2012, the University of Maryland's Board of Regents voted to withdraw from the ACC to join the <a href="/wiki/Big_Ten_Conference" title="Big Ten Conference">Big Ten Conference</a> effective in 2014.<sup id="cite_ref-131" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-131"><span>[</span>131<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Testudo">Testudo</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_Maryland,_College_Park&amp;action=edit&amp;section=25" title="Edit section: Testudo">edit</a>]</span></h2> 
     <div class="thumb tright"> 
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a href="/wiki/File:UMD_Testudo_Statue.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f8/UMD_Testudo_Statue.JPG/220px-UMD_Testudo_Statue.JPG" width="220" height="293" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f8/UMD_Testudo_Statue.JPG/330px-UMD_Testudo_Statue.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f8/UMD_Testudo_Statue.JPG/440px-UMD_Testudo_Statue.JPG 2x" /></a> 
       <div class="thumbcaption"> 
        <div class="magnify">
         <a href="/wiki/File:UMD_Testudo_Statue.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"><img src="//bits.wikimedia.org/static-1.22wmf9/skins/common/images/magnify-clip.png" width="15" height="11" alt="" /></a>
        </div> Statue of Testudo on campus
       </div> 
      </div> 
     </div> 
     <p>In 1932, <a href="/wiki/Curley_Byrd" title="Curley Byrd">Curley Byrd</a>?who served as the university's football and baseball coach, athletic director, and president?proposed adopting the <a href="/wiki/Diamondback_terrapin" title="Diamondback terrapin">diamondback terrapin</a> as a mascot. The first statue of Testudo cast in bronze was donated by the Class of 1933 and displayed on <a href="/wiki/U.S._Route_1_in_Maryland" title="U.S. Route 1 in Maryland">Baltimore Avenue</a> in front of <a href="/wiki/Ritchie_Coliseum" title="Ritchie Coliseum">Ritchie Coliseum</a>. However, the 300-pound sculpture was subjected to vandalism by visiting college athletic teams.<sup id="cite_ref-testudohist_132-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-testudohist-132"><span>[</span>132<span>]</span></a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Johns_Hopkins_%E2%80%93_Maryland_rivalry#Early_years" title="Johns Hopkins ? Maryland rivalry" class="mw-redirect">One such incident</a> occurred in 1947 when students from <a href="/wiki/Johns_Hopkins_University" title="Johns Hopkins University">Johns Hopkins University</a> stole the bronze statue and moved it to their campus. Maryland students traveled to <a href="/wiki/Baltimore" title="Baltimore">Baltimore</a> to retrieve it, laying siege to the house where it was hidden. Over 200 <a href="/wiki/Baltimore_Police_Department" title="Baltimore Police Department">city police</a> responded to quell the riot.<sup id="cite_ref-133" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-133"><span>[</span>133<span>]</span></a></sup> In 1949, University President Byrd was awakened by a phone call from a <a href="/wiki/University_of_Virginia" title="University of Virginia">University of Virginia</a> fraternity requesting that Testudo be removed from their lawn. Testudo was later filled with 700 pounds of cement and fastened to his pedestal to prevent future removals, but students at rival schools continued to vandalize it. It was moved to <a href="/wiki/Byrd_Stadium" title="Byrd Stadium">Byrd Stadium</a> in 1951. In the 1960s, Testudo was moved back to a spot in front of McKeldin Library. Some passersby consider it good luck to rub the statue, which has given its nose a shiny appearance. During finals week, students traditionally leave &quot;offerings&quot; to the statue for good luck.<sup id="cite_ref-134" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-134"><span>[</span>134<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-135" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-135"><span>[</span>135<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-autogenerated2_136-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-autogenerated2-136"><span>[</span>136<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-137" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-137"><span>[</span>137<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>In 1992 a duplicate statue was placed at Byrd Stadium, where the football team touch it for good luck as they pass by before games. Additional Testudo statues now sit outside of the Gossett Team House near the stadium; <a href="/wiki/Comcast_Center_(arena)" title="Comcast Center (arena)" class="mw-redirect">Comcast Center</a>, the school's basketball arena; the Riggs Alumni Center; and in the lobby of the <a href="/wiki/Adele_H._Stamp_Student_Union" title="Adele H. Stamp Student Union">Adele H. Stamp Student Union</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-autogenerated2_136-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-autogenerated2-136"><span>[</span>136<span>]</span></a></sup> In 1994, the <a href="/wiki/Maryland_General_Assembly" title="Maryland General Assembly">Maryland General Assembly</a> approved legislation to name the diamondback terrapin (<i>malaclemys terrapin terrapin</i>) as the official state reptile and the legally codified mascot of the University of Maryland.<sup id="cite_ref-138" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-138"><span>[</span>138<span>]</span></a></sup> Beginning in the 2000s (decade), the university promoted the slogan, &quot;Fear the Turtle&quot; as a rallying cry for school pride.<sup id="cite_ref-139" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-139"><span>[</span>139<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Notable_people">Notable people</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_Maryland,_College_Park&amp;action=edit&amp;section=26" title="Edit section: Notable people">edit</a>]</span></h2> 
     <div class="thumb tright"> 
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a href="/wiki/File:UMD_Riggs_Alumni_fountain.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d9/UMD_Riggs_Alumni_fountain.JPG/220px-UMD_Riggs_Alumni_fountain.JPG" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d9/UMD_Riggs_Alumni_fountain.JPG/330px-UMD_Riggs_Alumni_fountain.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d9/UMD_Riggs_Alumni_fountain.JPG/440px-UMD_Riggs_Alumni_fountain.JPG 2x" /></a> 
       <div class="thumbcaption"> 
        <div class="magnify">
         <a href="/wiki/File:UMD_Riggs_Alumni_fountain.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"><img src="//bits.wikimedia.org/static-1.22wmf9/skins/common/images/magnify-clip.png" width="15" height="11" alt="" /></a>
        </div> Fountain in front of the Riggs Alumni Center.
       </div> 
      </div> 
     </div> 
     <div class="thumb tright"> 
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a href="/wiki/File:A_Statue_of_Jim_Henson_and_Kermit_the_Frog_from_The_Muppets.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/25/A_Statue_of_Jim_Henson_and_Kermit_the_Frog_from_The_Muppets.jpg/220px-A_Statue_of_Jim_Henson_and_Kermit_the_Frog_from_The_Muppets.jpg" width="220" height="124" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/25/A_Statue_of_Jim_Henson_and_Kermit_the_Frog_from_The_Muppets.jpg/330px-A_Statue_of_Jim_Henson_and_Kermit_the_Frog_from_The_Muppets.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/25/A_Statue_of_Jim_Henson_and_Kermit_the_Frog_from_The_Muppets.jpg/440px-A_Statue_of_Jim_Henson_and_Kermit_the_Frog_from_The_Muppets.jpg 2x" /></a> 
       <div class="thumbcaption"> 
        <div class="magnify">
         <a href="/wiki/File:A_Statue_of_Jim_Henson_and_Kermit_the_Frog_from_The_Muppets.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"><img src="//bits.wikimedia.org/static-1.22wmf9/skins/common/images/magnify-clip.png" width="15" height="11" alt="" /></a>
        </div> Statue of Jim Henson and Kermit the Frog from The Muppets.
       </div> 
      </div> 
     </div> 
     <div class="rellink relarticle mainarticle">
      Main articles: 
      <a href="/wiki/List_of_University_of_Maryland,_College_Park_people" title="List of University of Maryland, College Park people">List of University of Maryland, College Park people</a> and 
      <a href="/wiki/President_of_the_University_of_Maryland,_College_Park" title="President of the University of Maryland, College Park" class="mw-redirect">President of the University of Maryland, College Park</a>
     </div> 
     <p>University attendees have achieved fame or notability across a variety of disciplines. Famous alumni include <a href="/wiki/Party_leaders_of_the_United_States_House_of_Representatives" title="Party leaders of the United States House of Representatives">House Minority Whip</a> <a href="/wiki/Steny_Hoyer" title="Steny Hoyer">Steny Hoyer</a>; <a href="/wiki/Google" title="Google">Google</a> co-founder <a href="/wiki/Sergey_Brin" title="Sergey Brin">Sergey Brin</a>; <a href="/wiki/The_Muppets" title="The Muppets">The Muppets</a> creator <a href="/wiki/Jim_Henson" title="Jim Henson">Jim Henson</a>;<i>The Wire</i> creator <a href="/wiki/David_Simon" title="David Simon">David Simon</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Seinfeld" title="Seinfeld">Seinfeld</a> producer <a href="/wiki/Larry_David" title="Larry David">Larry David</a>. Prominent alumni in business include <a href="/wiki/Jim_Walton_(journalist)" title="Jim Walton (journalist)">Jim Walton (journalist)</a>, President and CEO of <a href="/wiki/CNN" title="CNN">CNN</a>; <a href="/wiki/Kevin_Plank" title="Kevin Plank">Kevin Plank</a>, founder of the athletic apparel company <a href="/wiki/Under_Armour" title="Under Armour">Under Armour</a>;Leonard Kevin &quot;Len&quot; Bias was a first team All-American college basketball forward <a href="/wiki/Chris_Kubasik" title="Chris Kubasik">Chris Kubasik</a>, former President of <a href="/wiki/Lockheed_Martin" title="Lockheed Martin">Lockheed Martin</a>; <a href="/wiki/Carly_Fiorina" title="Carly Fiorina">Carly Fiorina</a>, former CEO of <a href="/wiki/Hewlett-Packard" title="Hewlett-Packard">Hewlett-Packard</a>; <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://encyclopedia.jrank.org/articles/pages/3973/Kerger-Paula-A.html">Paula Kerger</a>, President and CEO of the Public Broadcasting System (PBS); Telecommunications entrepreneur <a href="/wiki/Brian_Hinman" title="Brian Hinman">Brian Hinman</a>, Hamad Al Sayari, Former governor of the Saudi Arabian Central Bank(Saudi Arabia Monetary Agency) and Hugo Santana CEO of IBM Mexico.</p> 
     <div class="thumb tleft"> 
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;">
       <a href="/wiki/File:UMD_Arch_gateway.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6b/UMD_Arch_gateway.JPG/170px-UMD_Arch_gateway.JPG" width="170" height="227" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6b/UMD_Arch_gateway.JPG/255px-UMD_Arch_gateway.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6b/UMD_Arch_gateway.JPG/340px-UMD_Arch_gateway.JPG 2x" /></a> 
       <div class="thumbcaption"> 
        <div class="magnify">
         <a href="/wiki/File:UMD_Arch_gateway.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"><img src="//bits.wikimedia.org/static-1.22wmf9/skins/common/images/magnify-clip.png" width="15" height="11" alt="" /></a>
        </div> An arched gateway on campus
       </div> 
      </div> 
     </div> 
     <p>Television personality <a href="/wiki/Connie_Chung" title="Connie Chung">Connie Chung</a>; <a href="/wiki/E!" title="E!">E!</a> News reporter <a href="/wiki/Giuliana_Rancic" title="Giuliana Rancic">Giuliana Rancic</a> graduated with a bachelors degree from the <a href="/wiki/Philip_Merrill_College_of_Journalism" title="Philip Merrill College of Journalism">Philip Merrill College of Journalism</a>. <a href="/wiki/ESPN" title="ESPN">ESPN</a> reporters <a href="/wiki/Bonnie_Bernstein" title="Bonnie Bernstein">Bonnie Bernstein</a> and <a href="/wiki/Tim_Kurkjian" title="Tim Kurkjian">Tim Kurkjian</a> graduated from the <a href="/wiki/Philip_Merrill_College_of_Journalism" title="Philip Merrill College of Journalism">Philip Merrill College of Journalism</a>. <a href="/wiki/Scott_Van_Pelt" title="Scott Van Pelt">Scott Van Pelt</a>, also of ESPN, attended the Phillip Merrill College of Journalism, but finished a few credits short of graduation. Journalist <a href="/wiki/Carl_Bernstein" title="Carl Bernstein">Carl Bernstein</a>, who won the <a href="/wiki/Pulitzer_Prize_for_Public_Service" title="Pulitzer Prize for Public Service">Pulitzer Prize for Public Service</a> for his coverage of the <a href="/wiki/Watergate_scandal" title="Watergate scandal">Watergate scandal</a>, attended the University but also did not graduate. <a href="/wiki/Mark_Rosenker" title="Mark Rosenker">Mark Rosenker</a>, Former Chairman of the National Transportation Safety Board (NTSB) and now CBS NEWS Transportation Safety Analyst graduated with a bachelors of arts in radio and television. <a href="/wiki/Kiran_Chetry" title="Kiran Chetry">Kiran Chetry</a>, co-host of CNN's <a href="/wiki/American_Morning" title="American Morning">American Morning</a>, graduated with a bachelors of arts in broadcast journalism. <a href="/wiki/Heidi_Collins" title="Heidi Collins">Heidi Collins</a> of <a href="/wiki/CNN_Newsroom" title="CNN Newsroom">CNN Newsroom</a> graduated with a bachelors of science. Former Maryland governor <a href="/wiki/Harry_R._Hughes" title="Harry R. Hughes" class="mw-redirect">Harry R. Hughes</a> also attended. <a href="/wiki/Gayle_King" title="Gayle King">Gayle King</a>, editor-at-large for <i><a href="/wiki/O,_The_Oprah_Magazine" title="O, The Oprah Magazine">O, The Oprah Magazine</a></i>, graduated from Maryland with a degree in psychology. Television show host Bruce DePuyt, host of News Talk on <a href="/wiki/NewsChannel_8_(cable_channel)" title="NewsChannel 8 (cable channel)">NewsChannel8</a> graduated from Phillip Merrill College of Journalism.</p> 
     <p>Attendees within the fields of science and mathematics are: Nobel Laureates <a href="/wiki/Raymond_Davis_Jr." title="Raymond Davis Jr." class="mw-redirect">Raymond Davis Jr.</a>, 2002 winner in Physics; <a href="/wiki/Herbert_Hauptman" title="Herbert Hauptman" class="mw-redirect">Herbert Hauptman</a>, 1985 winner in Chemistry, and <a href="/wiki/Fields_Medal" title="Fields Medal">Fields Medal</a> winner <a href="/wiki/Charles_Fefferman" title="Charles Fefferman">Charles Fefferman</a>. Other alumni include <a href="/wiki/George_Dantzig" title="George Dantzig">George Dantzig</a>, considered the father of linear programming; late <a href="/wiki/NASA" title="NASA">NASA</a> <a href="/wiki/Astronaut" title="Astronaut">astronaut</a> <a href="/wiki/Judith_Resnik" title="Judith Resnik">Judith Resnik</a>, who died in the destruction of the <a href="/wiki/Space_Shuttle_Challenger" title="Space Shuttle Challenger">Space Shuttle Challenger</a> during the launch of mission <a href="/wiki/STS-51-L" title="STS-51-L">STS-51-L</a>; engineer <a href="/wiki/James_S._Albus" title="James S. Albus">James S. Albus</a>, founder of a division at the National Institute of Standards and Technology (NIST); and <a href="/wiki/NASA" title="NASA">NASA</a> Administrator <a href="/wiki/Michael_D._Griffin" title="Michael D. Griffin">Michael D. Griffin</a>.</p> 
     <p>Several donors have distinguished themselves for their sizable gifts to the University. Businessman <a href="/wiki/Robert_H._Smith" title="Robert H. Smith" class="mw-redirect">Robert H. Smith</a>, who graduated from the university in 1950 with a degree in accounting, has given over $45 million to the business school that now bears his name, and to the Clarice Smith Performing Arts Center, which bears his wife's name.<sup id="cite_ref-rhsmith_2005_140-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-rhsmith_2005-140"><span>[</span>140<span>]</span></a></sup> Construction entrepreneur <a href="/wiki/A._James_Clark" title="A. James Clark">A. James Clark</a>, who graduated with an engineering degree in 1950, has also donated over $45 million to the college of engineering, which also bears his name.<sup id="cite_ref-rhsmith_2005_140-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-rhsmith_2005-140"><span>[</span>140<span>]</span></a></sup> Another engineering donor, <a href="/wiki/Jeong_H._Kim" title="Jeong H. Kim">Jeong H. Kim</a>, earned his PhD from the university in 1991 and gave $5 million for the construction of a state-of-the-art engineering building.<sup id="cite_ref-141" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-141"><span>[</span>141<span>]</span></a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Philip_Merrill" title="Philip Merrill">Philip Merrill</a>, a media figure, donated $10 million to the College of Journalism.<sup id="cite_ref-142" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-142"><span>[</span>142<span>]</span></a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Robert_E._Fischell" title="Robert E. Fischell" class="mw-redirect">Robert E. Fischell</a>, physicist, inventor, and holder of more than 200 U.S. and foreign medical patents<sup id="cite_ref-143" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-143"><span>[</span>143<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-144" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-144"><span>[</span>144<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-MDDI_Fischell_145-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-MDDI_Fischell-145"><span>[</span>145<span>]</span></a></sup> donated $30 milion to the <a href="/wiki/A._James_Clark_School_of_Engineering" title="A. James Clark School of Engineering">A. James Clark School of Engineering</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-146" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-146"><span>[</span>146<span>]</span></a></sup> establishing the Fischell Department of Bioengineering.</p>
